2:36:2594:0:14:72:554:700:12:Times:12:Times:F:Parents' Beliefs About Their Children's Academic Ability: Implications for Educational Investments
2:37:2692:14:14:72:172:686:12:Times:12:Times:F:Rebecca Dizon-Ross
2:38:2710:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:F:NBER Working Paper No. 24610
2:39:2738:14:14:72:121:658:12:Times:12:Times:F:May 2018
2:40:2746:14:28:72:193:644:12:Times:12:Times:F:JEL No. D80,I20,I24,I25
2:41:2769:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:F:ABSTRACT
2:42:2777:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:F:Information  about  children’s  school  performance  appears  to  be  readily  available.  Do  frictions 
2:43:2882:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:F:prevent parents,   particularly low-income  parents,   from   acting   on   this   information   when 
2:44:2983:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:making decisions? I conduct a field experiment in Malawi to test this. I find that parents’ baseline 
2:45:3083:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:F:beliefs  about  their  children’s academic  performance  are  inaccurate.  Providing  parents  with 
2:46:3182:14:14:71:546:532:12:Times:12:Times:F:clear  and  digestible    academic    performance information    causes    them    to    update    their 
2:47:3286:14:14:71:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:F:beliefs   and correspondingly  adjust  their  investments:  they increase  the  school  enrollment  of 
2:48:3388:14:14:71:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:F:their  higher-performing  children,  decrease  the  enrollment  of  their lower-performing  children, 
2:49:3489:14:14:71:545:490:12:Times:12:Times:F:and  choose educational inputs that are more closely matched to their children’s academic level. 
2:50:3585:14:14:71:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:F:These  effects  demonstrate  the  presence  of  important  frictions  preventing  the  use  of available 
2:51:3689:14:42:71:511:462:12:Times:12:Times:F:information, with heterogeneity analysis suggesting the frictions are worse among the poor.
2:52:3780:42:14:71:171:420:12:Times:12:Times:F:Rebecca Dizon-Ross
2:53:3798:14:14:71:195:406:12:Times:12:Times:F:Booth School of Business
2:54:3822:14:14:71:178:392:12:Times:12:Times:F:University of Chicago
2:55:3843:14:14:71:222:378:12:Times:12:Times:F:5807 South Woodlawn Avenue
2:56:3869:14:14:71:161:364:12:Times:12:Times:F:Chicago, IL 60637
2:57:3886:14:14:71:123:350:12:Times:12:Times:F:and NBER
2:58:3894:14:250:71:181:336:12:Times:12:Times:F:rdr@chicagobooth.edu
2:59:3914:250:14:71:222:86:12:Times:12:Times:F:A data appendix is available at 
2:60:3946:14:14:71:282:72:12:Times:12:Times:F:http://www.nber.org/data-appendix/w24610
2:61:3986:14:14:71:357:58:12:Times:12:Times:F:A randomized controlled trials registry entry is available at 
2:62:4048:14:0:71:307:44:12:Times:12:Times:F:https://www.socialscienceregistry.org/trials/1808
3:63:4097:0:21:72:208:700:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:C:1Introduction
3:64:4110:21:18:95:539:679:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:It is commonly believed that one reason poor households remain poor is that they lack
3:65:4195:18:18:72:540:661:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:information that the rich possess (World Bank, 1998, 2008). Indeed, there is extensive ev-
3:66:4285:18:18:72:540:643:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:idence that providing information to poor individuals a↵ects their decision-making across
3:67:4374:18:18:72:540:625:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:many domains including health (e.g., Dupas (2011)), education (e.g., Jensen (2010)), and
3:68:4462:18:18:72:540:607:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:labor supply (e.g., Chetty and Saez (2009)). However, the vast majority of this evidence
3:69:4550:18:18:72:540:589:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:concerns information that even richer households may not have or use, such as the economic
3:70:4640:18:18:72:540:571:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:returns to education or market-level summary statistics. The question remains whether fric-
3:71:4731:18:18:72:540:553:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:tions prevent the poor from taking advantage of information that seems available to all, but
3:72:4823:18:18:72:493:535:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:which perhaps only those in richer households or countries can access and exploit.
3:73:4905:18:18:95:539:517:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:I examine these issues in a high-stakes environment: Parents making decisions about
3:74:4988:18:18:72:540:499:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:their children’s education. It is widely presumed that the correct educational decisions (such
3:75:5082:18:18:72:540:481:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:as whether to go to college or sign up for remedial tutoring) vary across individuals. Anec-
3:76:5174:18:18:72:540:463:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:dotally, in developing countries, the most important child-specific factor that determines
3:77:5264:18:17:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parents’ educational decisions is their children’s school performance. School performance
3:78:5353:17:18:72:540:428:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:information also appears to be freely available: schools worldwide deliver report cards to
3:79:5443:18:18:72:540:410:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parents that contain this information, and parents can also observe their children’s academic
3:80:5536:18:18:72:540:392:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:skills directly. And yet, there may be barriers preventing some parents from making use of
3:81:5626:18:18:72:540:374:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:this information (Banerjee et al., 2010). For example, parents in developing countries are of-
3:82:5720:18:18:72:540:356:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ten illiterate and may not be able to read or understand report cards. Limited education may
3:83:5812:18:18:72:540:338:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:also make it di-cult for parents to judge their children’s performance themselves, especially
3:84:5905:18:18:72:533:320:143:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f6:B:if their children go further in school than they did, as is common in developing countries.1
3:85:5997:18:18:95:539:302:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:This paper establishes that there are in fact substantial and consequential information
3:86:6084:18:18:72:540:284:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:frictions among poor parents regarding their children’s school performance.2First, I show
3:87:6173:18:18:72:540:266:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that many parents in a developing country context have inaccurate beliefs about their chil-
3:88:6264:18:18:72:540:248:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:dren’s school performance. Second, I demonstrate that parents base important educational
3:89:6352:18:18:72:540:230:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:decisions upon their inaccurate beliefs, even though they would like to use the correct infor-
3:90:6446:18:17:72:540:212:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:mation that is, in principle, readily available. Third, I use a randomized experiment to show
3:91:6539:17:18:72:540:195:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that a simple informational intervention can significantly alleviate the impacts of limited
3:92:6630:18:18:72:540:177:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:information: Providing information directly to parents in a clear and digestible way causes
3:93:6721:18:18:72:540:159:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parents to update their beliefs and adjust their decisions accordingly. Finally, I provide sug-
3:94:6816:18:18:72:540:141:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:gestive evidence on a link between information barriers and poverty, showing that poorer,
3:95:6905:18:16:85:539:123:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:1Free primary schooling in most developing countries only became widely available in the last 10-20 years,
3:96:7011:16:8:72:505:107:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:and the average adult in sub-Saharan Africa has fewer than 5 years of education (UNESCO, 2013).
3:97:7106:8:16:85:539:99:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:2Although this paper does not claim to distinguish between the various frictions at play, they may include
3:98:7212:16:12:72:540:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:parental illiteracy, limited parental ability to directly assess academic skills, the complexity of existing report
3:99:7327:12:0:72:343:71:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:cards, and problems with the report card delivery mechanism.
4:100:7388:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:less-educated parents have less accurate baseline beliefs than richer parents, and that both
4:101:7480:18:18:72:412:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:their beliefs and certain investments respond more to information.
4:102:7546:18:18:95:544:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:IdemonstratethesefindingsbyconductingarandomizedfieldexperimentinMalawi.
4:103:7618:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:The experiment delivers information to randomly-selected parents with children in primary
4:104:7707:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:school about their children’s “academic performance” (which hereafter refers to performance
4:105:7798:18:18:72:539:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:on achievement tests administered by schools over the previous term).3The information is
4:106:7886:18:18:72:539:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:delivered verbally and in a clear manner. I measure the e↵ect of the information on parents’
4:107:7978:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:beliefs, and on a broad range of their investments and decisions, including both a series of
4:108:8070:18:18:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:real-stakes investment options and decisions presented to parents through the experiment
4:109:8158:18:18:72:540:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:(“experimental outcomes”), and more traditional endline outcomes such as enrollment and
4:110:8245:18:18:72:517:528:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:attendance in school (“non-experimental outcomes”). The analysis proceeds as follows.
4:111:8330:18:18:95:539:510:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:I use baseline beliefs data to establish my first finding: that parents’ beliefs are inaccu-
4:112:8422:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:rate. On average, parents’ beliefs about academic performance diverge from true performance
4:113:8513:18:17:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:by more than one standard deviation of the performance distribution. When comparing two
4:114:8600:17:18:72:537:457:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of their children, one third of parents are mistaken about which child is higher-performing.
4:115:8692:18:18:95:543:439:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Inextcombineinformationonbelievedperformance,trueperformance,andinvestment
4:116:8766:18:18:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:decisions to test whether inaccurate beliefs a↵ect parents’ decisions. I establish my second
4:117:8858:18:18:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:finding – that, at baseline, parents base important decisions on their inaccurate beliefs – by
4:118:8952:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:demonstrating that, in the control group, the relationship between believed performance and
4:119:9043:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments is stronger than the relationship between true performance and investments. I
4:120:9132:18:18:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:then show my third finding – that the information intervention alleviates knowledge barriers
4:121:9224:18:18:72:540:331:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:– by showing that, in the treatment group, the relationship between true performance and
4:122:9312:18:18:72:540:313:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments becomes stronger, increasing to resemble the relationship in the control group
4:123:9402:18:18:72:540:295:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:betweenbelievedperformance and investment. This is because parents’ beliefs become more
4:124:9489:18:18:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:closely aligned with true performance, and they adjust their investments accordingly. The
4:125:9578:18:18:72:540:259:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:analyses show that student performance is an important input into parents’ decisions, but
4:126:9667:18:17:72:540:241:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that parents are often quite wrong about performance, resulting in important investment
4:127:9754:17:18:72:540:224:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:“mistakes” (i.e., wedges between how parents would like to allocate their investments given
4:128:9845:18:18:72:499:206:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:their children’s true academic performance, and how they allocate them in reality).
4:129:9928:18:18:95:543:188:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Iestablishtwobroadcategoriesofinvestmentmistakes.Thefirstismisallocationinthe
4:130:10005:18:18:72:540:170:143:g_d0_f9:143:g_d0_f4:B:levelof investment across children, i.e., cases in which the total amount invested in each
4:131:10095:18:18:72:540:152:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:child is not what parents want given children’s academic performance. I test for this using
4:132:10186:18:18:72:540:134:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:both enrollment in primary school, and an experimental outcome proxying for resources
4:133:10271:18:18:72:540:116:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:allocated towards secondary school. Providing information has impacts on both, causing
4:134:10357:18:18:72:540:98:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:reallocations towards higher-performing students in both cases. This suggests parents prefer
4:135:10449:18:15:85:539:80:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:3As described in Section 3, the Ministry of Education in Malawi requires all schools to send report cards
4:136:10554:15:0:72:523:65:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:to parents; thus, academic performance information should in theory be freely available in this context.
5:137:10659:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to allocate more years of schooling to their higher performers. This analysis clearly shows
5:138:10750:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that information frictions a↵ect investments; the implications for welfare then depend on
5:139:10839:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:whether there are other interacting market frictions, including whether parents are correct
5:140:10930:18:18:72:462:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:about the education production function, which I discuss later in the paper.
5:141:11006:18:18:95:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The second category of mistake I uncover is in thetypesof investment chosen for a
5:142:11087:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:given child, i.e., failures to tailor the specific input mix correctly to a child’s academic level
5:143:11185:18:18:72:545:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:–suchaspurchasinganadvancedtextbookforalow-performingchildwhentheremedial
5:144:11258:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:textbook would have benefited her more. Here I use several experimental outcomes, such as
5:145:11347:18:18:72:539:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:demand for books designed for students of di↵erent performance levels. The prediction is
5:146:11435:18:18:72:540:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that returns will be higher if the level of the selected book matches the level of the child’s
5:147:11529:18:18:72:540:528:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performance, and I find that providing information triples the closeness of the match. These
5:148:11621:18:18:72:540:510:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:types of parental decisions are now more relevant than ever in developing countries, since
5:149:11711:18:18:72:442:492:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the use of supplementary inputs is growing rapidly (Paviot et al., 2008).
5:150:11784:18:17:95:539:474:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Finally, I provide evidence on a link between poverty and information barriers, showing
5:151:11871:17:18:72:540:457:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that poorer, less-educated parents have less accurate baseline beliefs than richer parents, and
5:152:11966:18:18:72:516:439:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that they adjust their beliefs and certain investments more in response to information.
5:153:12053:18:18:95:540:421:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:This paper contributes to our understanding of how information frictions a↵ect deci-
5:154:12137:18:18:72:539:403:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:sions. A large literature shows that providing information to households a↵ects decision-
5:155:12226:18:18:72:539:385:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:making across many domains.4However these interventions have primarily delivered infor-
5:156:12313:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:mation that one might not expect households to know, even richer or well-informed house-
5:157:12401:18:18:72:539:349:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:holds. Some papers provide information that is di-cult or sometimes impossible to obtain,
5:158:12490:18:18:72:540:331:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:such as the (normally unobservable) economic returns to an activity (e.g., Jensen (2010)),
5:159:12580:18:18:72:540:313:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:or statistics that require another entity’s private information, such as school-average stu-
5:160:12672:18:18:72:539:295:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:dent performance or normally-unreleased data on student e↵ort in school (Andrabi et al.,
5:161:12760:18:18:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:2016; Bergman, 2016). Others deliver information that is in principle available but requires
5:162:12852:18:18:72:539:259:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:non-trivial e↵ort to obtain, such as personalized information about the cost of health plans
5:163:12944:18:17:72:540:241:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:or about the EITC schedule (Chetty and Saez, 2009; Kling et al., 2011). In contrast, this
5:164:13033:17:18:72:540:224:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:paper examines information that is seemingly readily available, showing that it is still not
5:165:13125:18:18:72:540:206:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:incorporated into the decisions made by the poor. This is important not just because it
5:166:13212:18:18:72:540:188:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:demonstrates a more surprising failure of optimization, but also because it provides evidence
5:167:13305:18:18:72:540:170:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of a channel through which the poor might remain poor: frictions that prevent them from
5:168:13392:18:18:72:527:152:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:using information that seems readily available to all, but that only the rich can leverage.
5:169:13483:18:18:95:539:134:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:This paper also contributes to the literature on information frictions in education. This
5:170:13572:18:18:72:540:116:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:literature has focused on misinformation about aggregate factors, such as the population-
5:171:13661:18:15:85:539:98:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:4e.g. Liebman and Luttmer (2015); Kling et al. (2011); Bhargava and Manoli (2015); Duflo and Saez
5:172:13758:15:0:72:473:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:(2000); Dupas (2011); Fitzsimons et al. (2016); Jamison et al. (2013); Beshears et al. (2015)
6:173:13852:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:average returns to education, school quality, or other features of the education system,5thus
6:174:13945:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:abstracting away from the fact that correct individual education decisions (such as whether
6:175:14036:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to go to college, or whether to invest in a remedial textbook) vary across individuals. Here,
6:176:14129:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:I shift focus from aggregates to the heterogeneity within the population, providing to my
6:177:14218:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:knowledge the first evidence using exogenous variation in beliefs to establish a causal link
6:178:14310:18:18:72:524:618:143:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f6:B:between misinformation about individual-level characteristics and investment decisions.6
6:179:14398:18:18:95:539:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The paper proceeds as follows. Section 2 motivates the empirical approach. Section 3
6:180:14482:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:describes the context and experimental design. Section 4 presents the results, and Section 5
6:181:14574:18:35:72:124:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:concludes.
6:182:14584:35:22:72:459:529:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:C:2Empirical approach for detecting mistakes
