8:283:22155:18:18:72:539:340:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:mation intervention that tells parents true performanceaand changes their mean beliefs
8:284:22241:18:18:72:539:322:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to equala.Ifattenuationsimplyresultedfromparentsallocatingsbased on some measure
8:285:22321:18:18:72:539:304:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:other than my performance measurea(i.e., if attenuation simply resulted from OVB and
8:286:22405:18:18:72:540:286:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:not parental mistakes), then parents’ investments would not change. If instead attenuation
8:287:22495:18:18:72:540:268:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:were the result of parents’ inaccurate beliefs aboutacausing them to make mistakes, then
8:288:22583:18:18:72:540:250:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:providing information onawould allow parents to correct their baseline mistakes and choose
8:289:22673:18:28:72:516:232:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:their preferred investments⇤(a), i.e., to invest along the preferred investment function:
8:290:22762:28:18:72:539:204:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f9:C:Prediction 2.If inaccurate beliefs cause parents to make investment mistakes at baseline,
8:291:22851:18:17:72:540:186:143:g_d0_f9:143:g_d0_f9:C:then information can change the slope of the actual investment function. In the case of
8:292:22938:17:28:72:296:169:143:g_d0_f9:143:g_d0_f9:C:baseline attenuation, the slope will increase.
8:293:22984:28:18:72:540:141:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:See Appendix C.1.2 for proof. An increase in the slope of the actual investment function as a
8:294:23077:18:18:72:540:123:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:result of providing information onathus shows us that parents’ baseline decisions were not
8:295:23167:18:18:72:540:105:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:optimal from their own perspective. Note that moving to a statement about welfare would be
8:296:23257:18:18:72:540:87:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:more complex, relying, for example, on whether the perceived production function is correct;
8:297:23349:18:0:72:540:69:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:I discuss this in detail later in the paper. Note also that the predictions and empirical test
9:298:23444:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:above focus on information’s impact on the slope of investments, not the average treatment
9:299:23534:18:22:72:504:690:143:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f6:B:e↵ect (ATE) of information, since ATE tend to understate information distortions.13
9:300:23617:22:18:95:539:668:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f4:A:Uncertainty:The earlier statement that a parent with mean beliefs↵iwould choose
9:301:23696:18:18:72:542:650:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:inputss⇤(↵i)dependsontheassumptionthattheutility-maximizingchoicedoesnotdepend
9:302:23774:18:18:72:539:632:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:on beliefs uncertainty,-2i. While this would be the case in some settings (e.g., if parents
9:303:23865:18:18:72:540:614:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:minimize a quadratic loss function), in others, having higher uncertainty could cause utility-
9:304:23959:18:18:72:540:596:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:maximizing investments to diverge froms⇤(↵i), and in particular, to become a function with
9:305:24049:18:17:72:540:578:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:aslopethatisflatterinmeanbeliefs↵i.Thisisbecausehigher-2imay cause a parent to
9:306:24127:17:18:72:540:561:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:hesitate to make her investments depend as strongly on her mean beliefs. See Appendix C.2
9:307:24216:18:18:72:539:543:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f19:B:for a framework yielding this prediction. This attenuation in the slope of investments on↵
9:308:24306:18:18:72:540:525:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:would then further attenuate the slope of investments onarelative to the case where there is
9:309:24398:18:18:72:543:507:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:perfect information abouta.Thus,onecanthinkofuncertaintyinbeliefsasasecondchannel
9:310:24479:18:35:72:535:489:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for baseline attenuation in the slope of investments ona,which I later test for empirically.
9:311:24571:35:22:72:382:454:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:C:3Context and experimental design
9:312:24603:22:18:95:539:432:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The setting for the experiment is Malawi. Overall, the education system in Malawi is
9:313:24687:18:18:72:540:414:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:similar to the systems in many countries in both sub-Saharan Africa and elsewhere, in terms
9:314:24778:18:18:72:540:396:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of the information given to parents as well as the overall structure. Primary school in Malawi
9:315:24872:18:18:72:540:378:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:covers grades 1-8. Although it has technically been free since 1994, it does involve expen-
9:316:24963:18:18:72:540:360:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ditures. Parents in the study sample spent an average of 1,750 Malawi Kwacha (MWK)
9:317:25045:18:18:72:540:342:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:annually per child, roughly 10.6 USD or 1% of annual household income. The main expendi-
9:318:25133:18:18:72:540:324:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:tures are uniforms (33% of total), informal but required school fees (22%), and supplemental
9:319:25225:18:18:72:540:306:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments such as school supplies, tutoring, and books (45%). The access rate to the first
9:320:25317:18:18:72:540:288:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:grade of primary school is above 95%, but dropouts are common in primary school. Sources
9:321:25405:18:18:72:540:270:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:vary, but all suggest the completion rate (conditional on enrolling) is less than 60% (World
9:322:25497:18:17:72:540:252:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Bank, 2010). Secondary school, covering grades 9-12, is not free, costing significantly more
9:323:25589:17:18:72:540:235:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:than primary school. Many children do not attend because of the high fees; annual fees for
9:324:25679:18:18:72:540:217:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:government secondary schools range from 5,000 - 10,000 MWK per year (30 - 60 USD, over 4
9:325:25767:18:18:72:540:199:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:times the median primary-school expenditures in the sample) (World Bank, 2010). Uniforms
9:326:25855:18:18:72:540:181:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and supplementary supplies are additional expenses. Secondary slots are also limited, with
9:327:25945:18:18:72:520:163:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:admissions governed by an achievement test administered at the end of primary school.
9:328:26030:18:18:95:539:145:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Similar to many other countries, schools are required to send report cards home each
9:329:26114:18:18:72:540:127:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:term with achievement test scores. The reports vary by school, but all are required to include
9:330:26208:18:18:72:540:109:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:average absolute test scores, and the corresponding grade on the standard Malawian grading
9:331:26298:18:15:81:539:91:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:13For example, if beliefs are inaccurate at the individual level but the population-level mean is correct,
9:332:26404:15:0:72:538:76:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:and investments are linear in performance, then parents might make mistakes but there would be no ATE.
10:333:26507:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:scale of 1-4. (Online App. H contains an example from the study sample.) However, the o-cial
10:334:26599:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:report cards are often hard for parents to understand, or do not reach them. According to
10:335:26688:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:baseline survey data, 64% of parents state that they do not know their child’s performance
10:336:26778:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:from the last report; the main stated reasons are that the parents (a) were unable to read
10:337:26868:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:or understand the report, or (b) did not receive it in the first place. Students are supposed
10:338:26961:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to deliver the reports, so children could either lose or choose not to deliver them: parents of
10:339:27056:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:students who performed badly are much less likely to receive the report. In addition, among
10:340:27147:18:18:72:539:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the parents whothinkthey know their children’s performance, anecdotally, some do not. For
10:341:27236:18:18:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:example, some misunderstand the grading scale (e.g., think a “1” is the highest grade when
10:342:27326:18:29:72:191:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:in fact it is the lowest).
10:343:27352:29:19:72:252:517:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:3.1Experimental design
10:344:27374:19:18:95:539:498:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The experiment delivers academic performance information to randomly selected par-
10:345:27456:18:18:72:539:480:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ents and measures the e↵ects on educational investments and decisions. Although the school
10:346:27546:18:18:72:540:462:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:report cards should ostensibly already deliver this information, as described above, the re-
10:347:27638:18:18:72:540:444:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:port card system does not succeed in conveying the information; the experiment presents
10:348:27725:18:17:72:540:426:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the information more clearly. To fit the framework presented in Section 2, the experiment
10:349:27814:17:18:72:540:409:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:should provide information about the individual-level trait on which parents’ educational
10:350:27903:18:18:72:540:391:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments depend. According to qualitative interviews, parents in Malawi think academic
10:351:27992:18:18:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performance (i.e., scores on school-administered exams) is the most important determinant
10:352:28081:18:18:72:540:355:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of both their investments and the returns to educational investments. If parents were wrong
10:353:28172:18:18:72:540:337:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:about the education production function, a second objective relevant for a scale-up would be
10:354:28264:18:18:72:540:319:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to use the trait most correlated withactualindividual-level returns. Academic performance
10:355:28353:18:18:72:540:301:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:likely also meets this second objective: It determines progression through school and selection
10:356:28448:18:18:72:539:283:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:into secondary school, thereby almost surely a↵ecting the returns to investment. “Innate”
10:357:28537:18:18:72:540:265:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ability is another possible determinant of returns, but, as has been extensively documented,
10:358:28629:18:18:72:539:247:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:it is di-cult to measure “innate” ability; any measure would represent some combination of
10:359:28719:18:21:72:433:229:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:innate ability and past inputs. (See Section 4.5 for further discussion.)
10:360:28792:21:18:95:539:208:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f4:A:Sample selection:The study worked with 39 schools in two districts (Machinga and
10:361:28872:18:18:72:540:190:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Balaka) in Malawi. Schools were selected randomly from the universe of primary schools,
10:362:28959:18:18:72:540:172:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:oversampling schools with high and low expected levels of parent education to increase
10:363:29045:18:18:72:540:154:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:heterogeneity in parent education within the sample. The study team first conducted a
10:364:29130:18:18:72:540:136:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:census at schools, mapping the sibling structures for all students in grades 2-6, which were
10:365:29222:18:18:72:540:118:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:chosen because they span most of primary school. Since one of the outcomes to be examined
10:366:29311:18:18:72:540:100:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:is inter-sibling tradeo↵s, multiple-sibling households were used as the sampling frame (fewer
10:367:29404:18:18:72:540:82:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:than 3% of households in Malawi with children have only one child). The team also gathered
10:368:29494:18:0:72:540:64:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:achievement test data from the most recent term (term 2 of the 2011-2012 school year) for
11:369:29584:0:18:72:190:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:use in the intervention.
11:370:29608:18:18:95:539:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Based on the test score and sibling data, a sample of 3,451 households with at least two
11:371:29696:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:children enrolled in grades 2-6 with test score data was drawn. For households with more
11:372:29784:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:than two children, two were randomly selected. Because one inclusion criterion was that
11:373:29871:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:children needed test score data, students who have the highest absence rates (and whose
11:374:29958:18:22:72:536:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parents might have the largest information problems) are under-represented in my sample.
11:375:30046:22:18:95:539:596:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f4:A:Randomization:I randomly assigned half the households in the sample to a treatment
11:376:30128:18:17:72:540:578:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:group that received information about their children’s test scores, and half to a control group,
11:377:30224:17:18:72:539:561:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:which did not.14The randomization was stratified on a test score measure (between-sibling
11:378:30313:18:18:72:540:543:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:score gap), and a proxy for parent education (the estimated literacy rate in the household’s
11:379:30405:18:22:72:487:525:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:village), since oneex antegoal was to look at heterogeneity by parent education.
11:380:30485:22:18:95:540:503:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f4:A:Eligibility interviews:Sample selection and randomization were based on data gath-
11:381:30567:18:18:72:540:485:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ered from students at school and on school administrative data. Household eligibility (i.e.,
11:382:30659:18:18:72:540:467:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:whether both siblings lived in the household and were still enrolled in school) was then
11:383:30747:18:18:72:540:449:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:verified through an eligibility questionnaire with parents. Among the 3,451 sampled house-
11:384:30837:18:17:72:540:431:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:holds, 21% of households were found to be ineligible during the parent interviews, leaving
11:385:30927:17:18:72:540:414:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:a sample of 2,716 eligible households. Of the 2,716 sampled and eligible households, 97%
11:386:31015:18:18:72:540:396:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:(2,634 households) were located at their homes, available, and consented to participate in
11:387:31105:18:18:72:540:378:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the baseline survey. Thus, the final experimental sample comprises 5,268 parent-child pairs.
11:388:31197:18:22:72:516:360:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Both eligibility and baseline survey completion are unrelated to treatment assignment.
11:389:31283:22:18:95:540:338:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f4:A:Baseline survey visit:Surveyors visited all sampled households and asked to speak
11:390:31364:18:18:72:539:320:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:with the parent who is the primary decision-maker about education.15Surveyors then con-
11:391:31451:18:18:72:540:302:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ducted a baseline survey, which included a module on education spending and beliefs about
11:392:31540:18:18:72:540:284:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:children’s test scores. While eliciting baseline beliefs about test scores, surveyors explained
11:393:31635:18:17:72:540:266:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the grading scale used by schools to parents; they also reviewed a sample report card with
11:394:31725:17:18:72:540:249:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the same format as those later delivered to the treatment group. This was done to aid the
11:395:31814:18:18:72:540:231:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:elicitation of beliefs and to hold knowledge of the grading scale and report card format con-
11:396:31907:18:18:72:540:213:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:stant across treatment groups. After the survey, during the same visit, surveyors conducted
11:397:31998:18:22:72:345:195:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the information intervention for the treatment group.
11:398:32051:22:18:95:540:173:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f4:A:Information intervention and report cards (Treatment group only):Surveyors
11:399:32125:18:16:81:539:155:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:14Half the treatment group was also assigned to receive an add-on intervention designed to test a hypothesis
11:400:32233:16:12:72:540:139:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:intended for study in separate work: that providing more detailed information would increase parental
11:401:32334:12:12:72:540:127:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:engagement, as measured through non-monetary and monetary investments. This group received additional
11:402:32435:12:12:72:540:115:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:skills information (e.g., whether their child could add 3-digit numbers, see Online Appendix I for sample).
11:403:32542:12:12:72:540:103:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:In this paper, I ignore this add-on treatment and pool the treatment households. I do not find that this
11:404:32646:12:8:72:309:91:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:treatment had an e↵ect on the pre-specified outcomes.
11:405:32699:8:16:81:539:83:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:15If that parent was unavailable, the surveyor spoke with the second parent if that parent was present and
11:406:32805:16:0:72:415:67:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:knowledgeable about educational decisions. If not, the surveyor returned later.
12:407:32885:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:walked parents in the treatment group through two report cards (one per child) describing
12:408:32974:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the academic performance of their children. The order was randomized. The reports showed
12:409:33062:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:children’s performance on all tests administered in the most recent school term, specifically:
12:410:33156:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the percent score (an absolute measure), the corresponding grade on the Malawian grading
12:411:33244:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:scale, and the within-class percentile ranking (see Online Appendix J for more details). The
12:412:33336:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:statistics were listed for the three subjects that Malawian educators deem most important
12:413:33425:18:18:72:544:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:–math,English,andChichewa,thelocallanguage–andfor“overall”(theaverageofthe
12:414:33499:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:three). The report card also showed the number of individual tests included in the averages;
12:415:33591:18:18:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the sample average is 4.5 tests. The correlation between students’ scores on the di↵erent
12:416:33680:18:18:72:503:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:individual tests is roughly 0.8 for overall performance, and 0.6 - 0.7 within subjects.
12:417:33767:18:18:95:539:528:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:A sample report card is presented in Appendix B. The format was chosen based on a
12:418:33848:18:18:72:540:510:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:series of focus groups, with the primary selection criterion being how well uneducated parents
12:419:33942:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:could understand it. Surveyors, who were trained on how to explain the information clearly,
12:420:34033:18:30:72:426:474:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:walked treatment parents through every number on the report cards.
12:421:34099:30:19:72:245:444:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:3.2Data and outcomes
12:422:34119:19:18:95:539:425:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The analysis uses several data sources, including data from surveys with parents and
12:423:34203:18:18:72:540:407:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:administrative data from schools. Online Appendix J.1 shows the survey questions that mea-
12:424:34293:18:17:72:540:389:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:sured beliefs and the experimental outcomes, and the scripts for the information intervention.
12:425:34387:17:18:95:539:372:143:g_d0_f9:143:g_d0_f4:A:(1) Baseline survey data:The baseline survey was rolled out immediately after term 2
12:426:34471:18:18:72:540:354:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of the school year ended in March 2012, and ran from April to June of 2012. The survey
12:427:34557:18:18:72:540:336:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:included modules on demographics, education spending, and the perceived returns to educa-
12:428:34646:18:18:72:540:318:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:tion. Mean beliefs about academic performance were measured by asking parents about the
12:429:34733:18:18:72:540:300:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:same performance metrics that were later delivered in the intervention report cards – average
12:430:34826:18:18:72:540:282:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:scores and percentile rankings on the term 2 school exams in math, English, Chichewa, and
12:431:34915:18:18:72:540:264:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:overall. We used the same measure later used in the intervention so that any gaps between
12:432:35004:18:18:72:539:246:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:believed and true performance represent belief inaccuracies, not di↵erences between mea-
12:433:35092:18:18:72:540:228:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:sures. Beliefs uncertainty was measured by asking parents to distribute tokens across bins
12:434:35182:18:18:72:262:210:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:representing score ranges (e.g., 0-20).
12:435:35221:18:18:95:540:192:143:g_d0_f9:143:g_d0_f4:A:(2) First endline survey - Endline beliefs and experimental outcomes:This survey was
12:436:35305:18:18:72:540:174:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:conducted immediately after the baseline survey and information intervention; see Figure
12:437:35393:18:17:72:544:156:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:2forthedatacollectiontimeline.Thiswasdoneforbudgetaryreasons,butdoeshavethe
12:438:35468:17:18:72:540:139:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:advantage that the outcomes were measured before parents had a chance to speak with
12:439:35551:18:18:72:540:121:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:others, allowing the outcomes to more cleanly reflect parents’ preferences, as opposed to the
12:440:35644:18:18:72:540:103:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:preferences of the people they talk to, including their children. Recall that there are two
12:441:35735:18:18:72:540:85:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:main categories of investment outcomes: (i) a series of real-stakes investment options and
12:442:35825:18:0:72:540:67:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:decisions presented to parents through the experiment (“experimental outcomes”); and (ii)
13:443:35916:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:more traditional endline outcomes measured during the year after the intervention, such as
13:444:36006:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:enrollment (“non-experimental” or longer-term outcomes). This survey measured the first
13:445:36093:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:category, which is described in more detail in Section 3.2.1 below, as well as endline beliefs.
13:446:36188:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:When measuring endline beliefs, because I wish to assess whether information a↵ects the
13:447:36275:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:beliefs underlying parents’ behavior, I want to know both whether (a) parents understood
13:448:36363:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and believed the information presented in the intervention, and (b) the information is relevant
13:449:36458:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for their decisions going forward. As a result, surveyors asked parents what score they thought
13:450:36553:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:their child would receive if he took an examthat same day. Asking about the previous-term
13:451:36642:18:18:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:scores as done in the baseline survey would only have measured (a), since those exams
13:452:36727:18:18:72:540:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:happened in the past; asking about a (hypothetical) same-day measure allows us to also
13:453:36813:18:18:72:540:528:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:assess (b). I refer to these beliefs as “endline beliefs.” Beliefs uncertainty was not measured
13:454:36908:18:18:72:261:510:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:at endline due to budget constraints.
13:455:36945:18:18:95:545:492:143:g_d0_f9:143:g_d0_f4:A:(3) Non-experimental (longer-term) outcomes:Ialsocollectedtwotypesofdatain
13:456:37019:18:17:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the year following the intervention: (i) a second endline survey of parents 1 year after the
13:457:37111:17:18:72:539:457:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:intervention (June-July 2013), which I use to examine treatment e↵ects on dropouts and
13:458:37197:18:18:72:540:439:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:expenditures, and (ii) administrative data on attendance gathered roughly 1 month after
13:459:37284:18:18:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the intervention (July 2012). These outcomes allow me to establish the policy relevance of
13:460:37374:18:18:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the findings. For the 1-year second endline data collection, given the very limited budget
13:461:37464:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:available, I focused on outcomes where (a) I expected results, and (b) data collection costs
13:462:37556:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:were lower. I thus focused on dropouts and expenditures, rather than academic performance.
13:463:37646:18:18:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Dropouts and expenditures are parental decisions that are easy to adjust, whereas academic
13:464:37736:18:18:72:539:331:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performance reflects many other factors. There was su-cient budget to include roughly 900
13:465:37825:18:18:72:540:313:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:households in the second endline survey sample. Of the households selected for the sample,
13:466:37915:18:18:72:540:295:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:98% (893) were successfully surveyed, balanced across treatment group. The administrative
13:467:38004:18:18:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:attendance data was gathered by giving schools templates to record the data for the month
13:468:38093:18:18:72:540:259:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:following the intervention, and was collected from 35% of the sample. During the attendance
13:469:38184:18:17:72:540:241:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:data collection, we were able to collect data on endline exams for 9% of the sample, which
13:470:38274:17:18:72:540:224:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:allows me to validate the accuracy of the baseline academic performance measure, but does
13:471:38363:18:18:72:540:206:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:not give su-cient statistical power to look at treatment e↵ects. See Online Appendix J.2 for
13:472:38455:18:22:72:440:188:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:more detail on the sample and data for the non-experimental outcomes.
13:473:38524:22:18:72:251:166:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:3.2.1Experimental outcomes
13:474:38550:18:18:95:539:148:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:During the first endline survey, surveyors presented parents with three real-stakes in-
13:475:38637:18:18:72:540:130:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:vestment decisions (the “experimental outcomes”). While the non-experimental outcomes
13:476:38722:18:18:72:540:112:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:are preferable from a policy-relevance perspective, these experimental outcomes have sev-
13:477:38811:18:18:72:540:94:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:eral advantages. The primary advantage is that they enable me to include outcomes that
13:478:38897:18:0:72:539:76:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:are designed to have clear predictions for how the e-cient investment depends on student
14:479:38987:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performance, allowing for a clean test of whether misinformation causes mistakes. They also
14:480:39078:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:allow me to include outcomes where the “preferred investment function” is homogeneous by
14:481:39166:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parental education, allowing me to cleanly test for whom inaccurate beliefs matter more.
14:482:39254:18:18:72:451:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Finally, they are very precise, allowing for detailed heterogeneity analysis.
14:483:39331:18:18:95:539:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The outcomes include a combination of monetary investments involving cash outlays,
14:484:39413:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and choices between free options. The latter allow us to abstract away from credit con-
14:485:39500:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:straints, which is useful for heterogeneity analysis as it enables cross-household comparisons
14:486:39594:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that are not confounded by household wealth. The outcomes also incorporate both smaller
14:487:39681:18:18:72:539:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments that primarily assess e↵ects on thetypesof investments parents choose, i.e.,
14:488:39769:18:18:72:540:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:whether they tailor the input mix correctly to their children’s needs, and a larger outcome
14:489:39860:18:21:72:473:528:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:designed to detect treatment e↵ects on thelevelof investment across children.
14:490:39937:21:18:95:540:507:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f4:A:Outcomes capturing thetypeof investment:The first decision presented to par-
14:491:40013:18:18:72:540:489:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ents is a choice among free workbooks with di↵erent di-culty levels. We gave parents four
14:492:40102:18:18:72:540:471:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:free books – an English and a math book for each of their two children. For each book, par-
14:493:40193:18:18:72:540:453:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ents were allowed to choose between three levels of di-culty: beginner, average, or advanced.
14:494:40286:18:18:72:539:435:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:The obvious prediction is that book di-culty choice will increase in perceived performance.
14:495:40377:18:18:95:539:417:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The second investment is the willingness to pay (WTP) for subject-specific remedial
14:496:40460:18:18:72:540:399:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:textbooks in math and English. WTP was evaluated using a Becker-DeGroot-Marschak
14:497:40540:18:18:72:540:381:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:(BDM) methodology, which gives respondents an incentive to report truthfully (see Online
14:498:40628:18:18:72:540:363:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Appendix K for description). The elicitation was real-stakes, with parents paying out-of-
14:499:40717:18:18:72:540:345:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:pocket for the textbooks using their own money, and the maximum price on the price list
14:500:40804:18:17:72:540:327:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:equal to the full market price. The average WTP for a book was substantial: 324 MWK (2
14:501:40890:17:18:72:540:310:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:USD), or roughly 20% of mean annual per-child educational expenditures. We use remedial
14:502:40977:18:18:72:540:292:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:textbooks (textbooks perceived by teachers as substitutes with performance). Thus, the
14:503:41063:18:18:72:540:274:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:prediction is that WTP will be higher for the subject in which parents think their child is
14:504:41154:18:18:72:540:256:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:doing worse; this was anex anteprediction, later confirmed by baseline survey questions
14:505:41241:18:18:72:507:238:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:showing that 95% of parents believe the textbooks are substitutes with performance.
14:506:41324:18:18:95:539:220:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Both the textbooks and free workbooks have clear predictions for parents’ beliefs about
14:507:41411:18:18:72:540:202:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the “right choice” (i.e., the perceived production function). An additional advantage is that
14:508:41504:18:18:72:539:184:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:both have clear predictions for theactualright choice and true production function. For
14:509:41591:18:18:72:540:166:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:example, the advanced workbook was designed specifically to be better for the higher per-
14:510:41680:18:18:72:540:148:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:formers in the sample. This enables a stronger argument that parental mistakes due to
14:511:41765:18:21:72:526:130:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:misinformation about child performance would lower actual (not just perceived) returns.
14:512:41852:21:18:95:539:109:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f4:A:Outcome capturing thelevelof investment across children:Secondary schooling
14:513:41927:18:18:72:540:91:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:is the first high-cost educational investment in Malawi. Few parents in the sample could
14:514:42015:18:0:72:539:73:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:a↵ord these fees for all of their children; many cannot for even a single child. My third
15:515:42106:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investment introduces a short-run, real-stakes proxy for secondary schooling. We conduct a
15:516:42196:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:lottery, in which the prize is four years of government secondary school fees for one child in
15:517:42290:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:every 100 households, worth roughly 120 - 240 USD at the time of the experiment. Parents
15:518:42378:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:were given nine tickets for the lottery and were asked to allocate the tickets across their two
15:519:42473:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:children. There are many “binary” choices in education where credit-constrained parents
15:520:42560:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:must choose between a lumpy investment in one child or the other, for example if parents
15:521:42648:18:18:72:539:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:can only a↵ord to send one child to secondary school or college. The lottery ticket allocation
15:522:42742:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:– and in particular, which child the parent allocates more tickets to – was designed to proxy
15:523:42835:18:18:72:220:564:143:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f6:B:for these types of decisions.16
15:524:42866:18:18:95:540:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:There are two main channels through which academic performance would a↵ect the ex-
15:525:42948:18:18:72:540:528:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:pected return of a lottery ticket. First, through the earnings return to secondary school: 95%
15:526:43042:18:18:72:540:510:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:(78%) of parents believe that secondary school increases the earnings of higher-performing
15:527:43132:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:students weakly (strictly) more than the earnings of lower-performing students, and, on av-
15:528:43223:18:17:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:erage, parents perceive the earnings increase to be 90% higher for a hypothetical child in
15:529:43313:17:18:72:540:457:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the top decile of performance than for one in the bottom decile. Second, since admissions is
15:530:43405:18:18:72:540:439:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:governed by performance on a standardized achievement test, the probability of admission
15:531:43493:18:18:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to secondary school increases with performance – a fact that 98% of parents are aware of.
15:532:43582:18:18:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Thus, the (perceived) expected value of the fees paid and the probability of attending in-
15:533:43672:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:crease with performance. Taking both channels together, a back-of-the-envelope calculation
15:534:43762:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:based on parents’ beliefs suggests that the perceived return is over 300% higher for students
15:535:43855:18:18:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:in the top vs. bottom performance decile.17Thus the prediction is that parents will allocate
15:536:43947:18:30:72:330:331:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:more lottery tickets to higher-performing children.
15:537:43998:30:19:72:332:301:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:3.3Summary statistics and balance
15:538:44031:19:18:95:538:282:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Table 1 presents summary statistics and tests for balance across the treatment and
15:539:44113:18:18:72:540:264:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:control groups. 77% of respondents are female, and 92% are the primary education decision
15:540:44202:18:18:72:540:246:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:maker in the household. Average levels of parental education are low, at 4.7 years. Households
15:541:44296:18:18:72:540:228:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:are large, with an average of 5 children. Sampled children were 12 years old on average,
15:542:44384:18:18:72:540:210:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:primarily aged 8 to 16, with 51% female. To test balance, I regress each variable on a dummy
15:543:44476:18:18:72:540:192:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for being in the treatment group. The di↵erences between the treatment and control groups
15:544:44565:18:18:72:540:174:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:are never large, with a joint test of equality failing to reject the null that all are 0 (p-value
15:545:44662:18:18:72:540:156:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:0.67) and only one of the 39 variables statistically significant at the 5% level: baseline math
15:546:44757:18:16:81:539:138:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:16Although a single ticket could have also accomplished this goal, I used multiple tickets to increase the
15:547:44863:16:12:72:540:122:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:power to detect small shifts and to allow me to make use of this lottery in a separate paper studying inequality
15:548:44975:12:12:72:540:110:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:aversion. As expected, most parents (74%) split their nine tickets as evenly as possible, consistent with an
15:549:45083:12:12:72:540:98:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:aversion to inequality between their children. The analysis thus reduces in most cases to analyzing which
15:550:45188:12:8:72:540:86:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:child the parents give their ninth ticket to, which proxies for the child they would choose in a binary choice.
15:551:45299:8:0:81:259:78:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:17See Online Appendix L for calculation.
16:552:45341:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:scores. To ensure this imbalance does not a↵ect the results, all regressions control for an
16:553:45432:18:34:72:524:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:academic performance measure, although the results are robust to omitting this control.
16:554:45519:34:21:72:245:656:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:C:4Empirical results
16:555:45537:21:18:72:540:635:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:I begin by showing that parents have inaccurate beliefs about their children’s academic per-
16:556:45629:18:18:72:540:617:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:formance. I then demonstrate, using first the experimental and then the non-experimental
16:557:45717:18:18:72:540:599:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:outcomes, that their belief inaccuracies cause them to make mistakes when making decisions.
16:558:45808:18:18:72:540:581:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Finally, I provide evidence linking information frictions with poverty, and discuss the impli-
16:559:45902:18:29:72:540:563:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:cations of information frictions for welfare and the average level of investment in education.
16:560:45996:29:20:72:154:534:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:4.1Beliefs
16:561:46006:20:17:72:540:514:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:Result 1A: Parents’ beliefs about academic performance appear to be inaccurate.
16:562:46085:17:18:95:539:497:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Data from the baseline survey can be used to assess the accuracy of parents’ beliefs about
16:563:46175:18:18:72:540:479:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:their children’s “academic performance,” i.e., scores on school-administered exams the prior
16:564:46267:18:18:72:540:461:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:term. Figure 3(a) presents the average of the absolute value of the gap between parents’
16:565:46355:18:18:72:540:443:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:mean beliefs about their children’s academic performance and their children’s true academic
16:566:46446:18:18:72:539:425:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performance. Scores are absolute percentages, expressed on a scale from 0 to 100.18The
16:567:46532:18:18:72:536:407:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:graph shows the treatment and control groups separately to demonstrate baseline balance.
16:568:46620:18:17:95:539:389:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The average gap is large: 20 points, or 1.2 standard deviations of the performance dis-
16:569:46707:17:18:72:540:372:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:tribution for overall performance. Table 1, Panel F shows that mean beliefs about individual
16:570:46799:18:18:72:540:354:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:subjects like math, between-subject performance (math vs. English), and the between-sibling
16:571:46890:18:18:72:540:336:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:gap are also inaccurate. Beliefs about the between-sibling gap diverge from the true gap by
16:572:46981:18:18:72:540:318:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:1.1 std. dev. on average, with 31% of parents wrong about which of their own children is
16:573:47069:18:18:72:472:300:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:higher-scoring. While parents overestimate on average, 21% of parents do not.
16:574:47146:18:18:95:539:282:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:As described in Section 2, these belief inaccuracies should cause mean beliefs to not
16:575:47231:18:18:72:540:264:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:move 1-to-1 with true scores and instead to be an attenuated function of true scores. Figure
16:576:47323:18:18:72:540:246:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:3(b) substantiates this for overall performance with a local linear regression of mean beliefs
16:577:47417:18:18:72:540:228:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:on true performance: the slope is visually less than 1. The attenuation in the slope captures
16:578:47510:18:18:72:540:210:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the fact that the correlations between believed and true performance are low: 0.3 for overall
16:579:47603:18:18:72:540:192:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performance, as depicted in the graph, and 0.2-0.3 for performance in the individual subjects
16:580:47696:18:18:72:540:174:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:like math. Since these tests determine progression through school, these inaccuracies are likely
16:581:47792:18:16:72:285:156:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:relevant for a broad range of investments.
16:582:47834:16:16:81:540:140:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:18The online appendix shows that the main results are robust to using relative performance (within-
16:583:47933:16:12:72:540:124:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:class percentiles) instead of absolute performance. (Tables G.1, G.2, and G.3.) In my sample, absolute and
16:584:48039:12:12:72:539:112:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:relative performance are highly correlated (0.8). Rogers and Feller (2016) compare the e↵ects of relative versus
16:585:48151:12:12:72:540:100:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:absolute information about student absence rates from school; such a comparison was not a goal of this study.
16:586:48260:12:12:72:540:88:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:That being said, Online Appendix G.18 shows results when both measures are analyzed simultaneously, and
16:587:48363:12:12:72:540:76:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:parents seem to respond more to absolute than to relative information. Online Appendix J.4 discusses this
16:588:48468:12:0:72:503:64:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:in more detail, as well as explaining the other reasons that the analysis uses absolute performance.
17:589:48570:0:18:95:539:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:One natural question is whether these “inaccuracies” in beliefs simply reflect noise in
17:590:48657:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the performance measure. The data suggest otherwise. The correlation between tests taken
17:591:48745:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:during the term is 0.8 for overall performance, and 0.6-0.7 within subjects, which suggest
17:592:48835:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:high test reliability; these are notably higher than the correlations between parents’ beliefs
17:593:48929:18:18:72:539:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and the term-average scores (0.2-0.3). I also have data onfuturetest scores for a small
17:594:49016:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:subset of the sample which shows that baseline test scores are nine times more predictive of
17:595:49108:18:18:72:539:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:future test scores than parents’ baseline beliefs are.19Moreover, we can use the experiment
17:596:49199:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:itself to provide more evidence on this issue: If providing information to parents causes them
17:597:49293:18:18:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to update their beliefs, it suggests that parents themselves believe that there is additional
17:598:49386:18:22:72:508:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:meaningful content in the information that was not reflected in their baseline beliefs.
17:599:49473:22:18:72:355:524:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:Result 1B: Providing information a↵ects beliefs.
17:600:49521:18:18:95:543:506:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Inowaskwhetherinformationchangesbeliefsanddecreasesattenuationbylookingat
17:601:49594:18:17:72:540:488:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the impact of information on mean beliefs measured at endline. Recall that, unlike beliefs
17:602:49684:17:18:72:540:471:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:measured at baseline, the beliefs question asked at endline was not asking about last-term
17:603:49774:18:18:72:540:453:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:test scores; instead, it asked how well parents thought their child would do on a hypothetical
17:604:49868:18:18:72:540:435:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:test taken that same day. The prediction is thus that providing information should decrease
17:605:49959:18:18:72:540:417:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the gap between parents’ endline beliefs and their child’s last-term scores, as their posterior
17:606:50054:18:18:72:540:399:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:beliefs move in the direction of the signal; the gap however should not fall to 0, unless parents
17:607:50151:18:18:72:540:381:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:place no weight on other factors (e.g., their assessment of their child’s recent progress). Fig-
17:608:50247:18:18:72:540:363:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ure 3(c) graphs the absolute value of the gap between true baseline (last-term) performance
17:609:50338:18:18:72:540:345:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and endline beliefs, separately by treatment group. Consistent with Bayesian updating, in-
17:610:50428:18:18:72:540:327:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:formation cuts the gap nearly in half. Figure 3(d) shows that attenuation correspondingly
17:611:50517:18:18:72:540:309:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:decreases: the slope of endline beliefs on true baseline scores is over twice as steep for the
17:612:50611:18:18:72:284:291:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:treatment group as for the control group.
17:613:50652:18:18:95:539:273:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:I formally test whether information increases the slope of endline beliefs by running the
17:614:50741:18:32:72:175:255:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:following regression:
17:615:50762:32:33:159:540:223:143:g_d0_f10:143:g_d0_f4:A:yij=c0+c1Aij⇥T reati+c2Aij+c3T reati+c04Xij+"ij(1)
17:616:50812:33:18:72:539:190:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:whereiindexes households,jindexes siblings,yijis the parent’s endline beliefs about overall
17:617:50903:18:18:72:540:172:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:academic performance,Aijis baseline overall academic performance,T reatiis an indicator
17:618:50990:18:19:72:540:154:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for being assigned to the treatment group, andXijis a vector of control variables.20Standard
17:619:51082:19:15:81:539:135:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:19See Online App. Table G.4 for a regression using control group data: the coe-cients on current test
17:620:51183:15:12:72:539:120:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:scores and beliefs are 0.74 and 0.08, respectively. Misunderstanding the di-culty of the grading scale also
17:621:51290:12:9:72:540:108:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:does not drive the results: the patterns are similar for within-class percentile ranks (Online App. Table G.1).
17:622:51401:9:15:81:539:99:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:20Results are robust to excluding the controls (see Online Appendix Tables G.5 and G.6). Controls include
17:623:51506:15:12:72:540:84:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:school fixed e↵ects (FE), the between-child score gap, average parental years of education, child and parent
17:624:51614:12:0:72:540:72:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:gender, and grade FE. This includes all variables underlying the stratification but not the stratum FE
18:625:51718:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:errors are clustered at the household level. Table 2, col. (1) confirms the increase in slope
18:626:51811:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:(c1>0). Information thus has a statistically significant “first stage” e↵ect on beliefs, allowing
18:627:51908:18:31:72:532:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:us to use the experiment to examine the e↵ects of information and beliefs on investments.
18:628:51997:31:18:72:336:641:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:4.2Results: Experimental outcomes
18:629:52030:18:18:95:543:623:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Ifirstexaminethe“experimentaloutcomes,”i.e.,theinvestmentdecisionspresentedto
18:630:52107:18:18:72:540:605:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parents in the first endline survey, which allow me to cleanly document investment mistakes,
18:631:52199:18:18:72:540:587:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:before turning to the “non-experimental outcomes” to establish greater policy relevance. I
18:632:52289:18:18:72:540:569:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:begin by using data from the control group to provide motivating evidence of mistakes, and
18:633:52379:18:22:72:312:551:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:then present the information treatment e↵ects.
18:634:52425:22:18:72:540:529:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:Result 2A: Control group parents attempt to tailor their investments to perfor-
18:635:52504:18:18:72:204:511:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:mance, but partly fail.
18:636:52527:18:18:95:539:493:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Data from the control group can be used to study how baseline parental investments
18:637:52609:18:18:72:540:475:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:depend on parents’ beliefs about performance. This can give us insight into parents’ preferred
18:638:52703:18:18:72:540:457:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investment function and the likely production function that they have in mind. We can then
18:639:52793:18:18:72:540:439:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:compare this with how investments vary withtrueperformance. A divergence between the
18:640:52877:18:18:72:450:421:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:two relationships would suggest that inaccurate beliefs a↵ect investments.
18:641:52951:18:17:95:539:403:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Figure 4 compares the preferred investment function (investments plotted against be-
18:642:53035:17:18:72:540:386:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:lieved performance – the dashed lines) with the actual investment function (investments
18:643:53122:18:18:72:540:368:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:plotted against true performance – the solid lines). Note that the y-axes for both lines rep-
18:644:53215:18:18:72:539:350:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:resent investments, but the x-axes di↵er. Both are locally linear regressions using control
18:645:53306:18:18:72:520:332:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:group data. I first interpret the preferred functions. I then compare them to the actual.
18:646:53395:18:18:95:539:314:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Panel (a) of Figure 4 presents the results for math and English workbook di-culty
18:647:53476:18:18:72:540:296:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:choices graphically. Recall that for each book, parents could choose from 3 di↵erent di--
18:648:53565:18:18:72:539:278:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:culty levels. The y-axis represents the chosen di-culty level, with the three di↵erent levels
18:649:53658:18:18:72:539:260:143:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f6:B:parametrized as 0/1/2 for simplicity, but the results are robust to other parametrizations.21
18:650:53751:18:18:72:543:242:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Ifocusfirstonthedashedlines,whichrepresentsparents’preferredchoicegiventheirbeliefs
18:651:53834:18:18:72:540:224:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:about their child’s math or English score, represented by the x-axis. The obvious prediction
18:652:53926:18:18:72:540:206:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:is that book di-culty choice should increase in believed performance, and indeed, consistent
18:653:54018:18:18:72:521:188:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:with this prediction, the dashed lines for both English and math slope steeply upwards.
18:654:54105:18:18:95:539:170:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Panel (b) of Figure 4 presents similar results for the second investment, the willingness
18:655:54194:18:17:72:540:152:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to pay (WTP) for subject-specific textbooks in math and English. Because the textbooks
18:656:54280:17:18:72:540:135:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:are remedial, the prediction is that WTP will be higher for the subject in which parents
18:657:54368:18:23:72:539:117:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:think their child is doing worse. The use of the between-subject WTP (math-English)
18:658:54451:23:11:72:540:94:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:themselves; I pre-specified that I would not control for stratum FE because some strata are very small: 15%
18:659:54558:11:9:72:540:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:of observations would be lost if I included stratum FE. But, the results are robust to including stratum FE.
18:660:54666:9:0:81:485:74:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:21See Online Appendix Tables G.7 and G.8 for robustness to an ordered probit specification.
19:661:54759:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:holds constant other factors such as the child’s overall performance, which is advantageous
19:662:54850:18:18:72:305:690:143:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f6:B:for this test as it provides clean predictions.22
19:663:54899:18:18:95:539:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:In Panel (b), as in Panel (a), the dashed lines are the preferred investment lines. The
19:664:54986:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:x-axis shows beliefs about performance in English relative to math. The y-axis shows the
19:665:55074:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:log of WTP for the math textbook minus the log of WTP for the English textbook;23for
19:666:55158:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:presentation purposes, English is flipped relative to math on the y-axis, so that the prediction
19:667:55254:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:is that the line will have a positive slope. The dashed line slopes steeply upwards, consistent
19:668:55349:18:18:72:523:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:with the prediction that WTP increases the further behind a child is in a given subject.
19:669:55437:18:18:95:539:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Panel (c) of Figure 4 shows the secondary school lottery ticket allocation results. The
19:670:55524:18:18:72:539:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:dashed line plots the di↵erence in tickets allocated to the older versus the younger child in
19:671:55617:18:18:72:539:528:143:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f6:B:the pair, with the x-axis the gap in perceived scores between the older and younger child.24
19:672:55709:18:18:72:539:510:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Consistent with theex anteprediction that allocating more tickets to higher-performers
19:673:55795:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:yields higher returns, the line slopes upwards: Parents give more tickets to the child they
19:674:55886:18:17:72:210:474:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:think is higher-performing.
19:675:55913:17:18:95:539:457:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:I now compare the slope of the preferred investment functions just discussed with the
19:676:55998:18:18:72:540:439:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:slopes of theactualinvestment functions, depicted by the solid lines in Figure 4. The solid
19:677:56089:18:18:72:539:421:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:lines have the same y-axes as the dashed lines, but di↵erent x-axes: Their x-axes are true
19:678:56179:18:18:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performance instead of believed performance. The prediction is that if parents base their in-
19:679:56272:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:vestments on their inaccurate beliefs, then the slope of their investments on true performance
19:680:56366:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:will be attenuated relative to the slope on beliefs. And, in fact, the graphs show precisely this
19:681:56463:18:18:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:pattern: The slopes on true performance are only 15-40% as large as the slopes on beliefs.
19:682:56553:18:18:72:540:331:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:This suggests that parents try to tailor their investments to performance, but that their
19:683:56642:18:18:72:540:313:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:inaccurate beliefs prevent them from doing so. Since returns depend ontrueperformance, if
19:684:56731:18:18:72:540:295:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parentsknewthat, say, their child had a math score of 80, they would choose the highest dif-
19:685:56823:18:18:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ficulty book for him, but many parents do not know that and so fail to choose their preferred
19:686:56916:18:18:72:540:259:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:option. This evidence is suggestive, however, not causal; both beliefs and performance could
19:687:57008:18:17:72:540:241:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:be correlated with other factors that determine investments. An experiment, in contrast, can
19:688:57100:17:18:72:540:224:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:establish causality: I can test whether information undoes the attenuation. It is this I turn
19:689:57193:18:16:81:540:206:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:22Theex anteplan was to analyze within-child, between-subject WTP, since surveys with teachers showed
19:690:57294:16:12:72:539:190:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:that teachers universally think that, within child, the remedial textbooks have higher returns in asubjectin
19:691:57402:12:12:72:540:178:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:which the child is behind. In contrast, teachers have more mixed opinions about whether remedial textbooks
19:692:57508:12:12:72:539:166:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:have higher returns for achildwho is behind in a subject relative to a child who is ahead. These mixed
19:693:57610:12:12:72:540:154:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:opinions reflect the fact that a child who is behind in one subject also has lower performance on average,
19:694:57716:12:12:72:540:142:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:and so might be less inclined to use a textbook, even a remedial one, since he/she may be more likely to
19:695:57820:12:8:72:504:130:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:drop out of school, etc. The within-child, between-subject comparison holds those factors constant.
19:696:57919:8:16:81:539:122:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:23Only 6% of observations are 0’s, which I replace with the log of 10% of the lowest price list value, but
19:697:58025:16:8:72:523:106:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:the results are robust to using other values (e.g., 50%), dropping the 0’s, or using levels instead of logs.
19:698:58133:8:15:81:539:98:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:24Since the lottery is a within-household allocation, to depict it graphically, we need to order the two chil-
19:699:58243:15:12:72:540:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:dren in some way. Parents identified age in focus groups as the second most important factor for investment
19:700:58350:12:0:72:453:71:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:(behind performance), so I order using age, but the graphs look similar with any order.
20:701:58439:0:22:72:112:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to next.
20:702:58447:22:18:72:491:686:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:Result 2B: Information substantially increases the slope of investments
20:703:58518:18:18:95:543:668:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Inowusetheinformationexperimenttotestwhetherinformationincreasestheslopeof
20:704:58592:18:18:72:540:650:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments on actual performance. Figure 5 shows locally linear regressions of investments
20:705:58683:18:18:72:540:632:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:on true performance for the treatment group (dashed line) and control group (solid line).
20:706:58772:18:18:72:540:614:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Both lines have true performance as the x-axis. Note that Figure 4 examined only the control
20:707:58864:18:18:72:540:596:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:group, and thus the solid lines in Figures 4 and 5 are identical, as they depict the same data.
20:708:58959:18:18:95:539:578:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The figures confirm that information frictions cause mistakes: For all three investments
20:709:59047:18:18:72:540:560:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:considered, the information treatment substantially increases the slope of the investment
20:710:59136:18:18:72:540:542:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:functions. I perform a formal test of the change in slope by estimating equation 1 using the
20:711:59228:18:18:72:540:524:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:experimental outcomes as the outcome variables, and using the relevant academic perfor-
20:712:59315:18:18:72:540:506:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:mance metric asAij(e.g., math for math workbooks). The prediction is that the information
20:713:59404:18:17:72:540:488:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:treatment makes the slope steeper, so thatc1>0(withc1the coe-cient onAij⇥T reati).
20:714:59486:17:18:72:544:471:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:The key prediction regardsc1;c3,thecoe-cientonT reati,isnotparticularlymeaningful
20:715:59567:18:18:72:539:453:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:as it is just driven by the scaling of theAijvariable, representing the treatment e↵ect for
20:716:59658:18:18:72:539:435:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:those for whomAij=0fortheparticularAijmeasure used in that regression. For example,
20:717:59741:18:18:72:540:417:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for the textbook regression, it is the treatment e↵ect for those for whom math and English
20:718:59831:18:18:72:351:399:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performance are the same (i.e.,math-English=0).
20:719:59878:18:18:95:539:381:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Columns (2) through (5) of Table 2 present the results for the math and English work-
20:720:59963:18:18:72:539:363:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:book di-culty choices; the log of WTP for the math textbook minus the log of WTP for the
20:721:60051:18:18:72:540:345:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:English textbook; and the secondary school lottery tickets received. Since secondary school
20:722:60142:18:18:72:540:327:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:lottery tickets are inherently a within-household allocation (one child’s allocation fully deter-
20:723:60239:18:18:72:540:309:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:mines the other’s), the lottery regression is estimated with a household fixed e↵ect. Consistent
20:724:60335:18:18:72:539:291:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:with the graphical evidence, across all outcomes,c1is positive and statistically significant.
20:725:60428:18:18:72:539:273:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:The magnitudes are large: Comparing the coe-cient onScore(slope in the control group)
20:726:60513:18:18:72:539:255:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:with the sum of the coe-cients onScoreandT reat⇥Score(slope in the treatment group),
20:727:60597:18:17:72:539:237:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:information causes investments to become 3-6timesmore steeply aligned with performance
20:728:60683:17:18:72:540:220:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:across the various investments, i.e., the slopes increase by roughly 200-500%. This suggests
20:729:60775:18:18:72:372:202:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that parents were making substantial mistakes at baseline.
20:730:60833:18:18:95:539:184:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:One question is whether demand e↵ects play a role in the patterns seen here. Although
20:731:60918:18:18:72:539:166:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:demand e↵ects should a↵ect both treatment and control groups and should thus not directly
20:732:61007:18:18:72:539:148:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:account for the treatment e↵ects, demand e↵ects could cause all parents, treatment and con-
20:733:61098:18:18:72:539:130:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:trol, to choose investments more closely tied to perceived academic performance (i.e., a↵ect
20:734:61190:18:18:72:539:112:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the slope of thepreferredinvestment function). The use of real stakes for all investments,
20:735:61280:18:18:72:540:94:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:which is the standard approach to address demand e↵ects, helps assuage this concern. More-
20:736:61370:18:0:72:540:76:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:over, treatment e↵ects on the longer-term outcomes can also mitigate the concern, since
21:737:61459:0:31:72:522:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:these outcomes should not be subject to demand e↵ects. I analyze these outcomes next.
21:738:61544:31:19:72:468:677:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:4.3Results: Non-experimental (longer-term) outcomes
21:739:61595:19:18:95:539:658:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The above results demonstrate that inaccurate beliefs cause parents to make mistakes
21:740:61679:18:17:72:540:640:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:when allocating educational investments. An open question, however, is the relevance for de-
21:741:61771:17:18:72:540:623:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:cisions outside of the experimental environment. I next turn to longer-run, non-experimental
21:742:61863:18:18:72:540:605:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:outcomes to show that information frictions are also relevant for outcomes that map more
21:743:61951:18:18:72:540:587:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:directly to the policy outcomes of interest. However, theex antepredictions for the preferred
21:744:62044:18:22:72:434:569:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investment function are generally not as clear,25and precision is lower.
21:745:62116:22:18:72:493:547:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:Result 3: Information a↵ects the slope of non-experimental investments
21:746:62186:18:18:95:543:529:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Iagainexaminethee↵ectofinformationontheslopeofinvestments.PanelAofTable
21:747:62257:18:18:72:544:511:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:3presentsestimationsofequation1,allusingoverallscoresastheperformancemeasure.To
21:748:62336:18:18:72:540:493:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:aid in interpretation, Panel B shows estimates using binary regressors for both performance
21:749:62427:18:18:72:540:475:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and education, specifically: indicators for whether a student has above-median score and for
21:750:62519:18:18:72:540:457:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:whether a household has above-median parent education. I consider three outcomes: primary
21:751:62608:18:18:72:540:439:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:school enrollment (dropouts), attendance, and expenditures. Of the three, primary school
21:752:62696:18:18:72:539:421:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:enrollment, which likely proxies most closely for the overalllevelof investment, provides the
21:753:62789:18:17:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:cleanest test: Consistent with the literature, most parents believe additional years of school-
21:754:62884:17:18:72:540:386:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ing are more valuable for higher-performing children, whereas parental beliefs about the
21:755:62972:18:18:72:540:368:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:complementarity of expenditures or attendance with performance, as elicited in interviews,
21:756:63062:18:18:72:539:350:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:vary widely across parents. The literature on attendance and expenditures is also limited,
21:757:63152:18:18:72:540:332:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and there is little reason to expect the production function to be the same as for years of
21:758:63243:18:18:72:540:314:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:schooling. For example, conditional on having a child enrolled in school, parents may need
21:759:63333:18:18:72:442:296:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to invest more in their lower-performing children to keep them on track.
21:760:63405:18:18:95:539:278:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Column (1) shows the primary school enrollment results. Consistent with the fact that
21:761:63490:18:18:72:540:260:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:nearly all parents believe years of schooling are a complement with academic performance,
21:762:63579:18:18:72:540:242:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:information increases the slope of the investment function. High-performing students in the
21:763:63670:18:18:72:540:224:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:treatment group are more likely to be enrolled in school one year later, while low-performing
21:764:63763:18:18:72:540:206:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:students are less likely to be enrolled. The change in the slope in Panel A is significant at
21:765:63856:18:18:72:540:188:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the 1% level.26Panel B shows that the magnitudes are economically meaningful. Among
21:766:63939:18:15:81:539:170:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:25It is also harder to use control group data to generate predictions for the production function parents have
21:767:64049:15:12:72:540:155:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:in mind; compared with the experimental outcomes, these outcomes have more omitted determinants, making
21:768:64152:12:12:72:540:143:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:the observational regressions harder to interpret. However, we can still use the information treatment e↵ects
21:769:64261:12:8:72:528:131:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:themselves to infer the perceived complementarity/substitutability of the investments with performance.
21:770:64364:8:16:81:539:123:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:26Many evaluations use self-reported enrollment as the outcome of interest (e.g., Bourguignon et al., 2003;
21:771:64471:16:12:72:540:107:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:Schultz, 2004), but Baird and ̈Ozler (2012) show that self-reported and school data do not always match. I
21:772:64577:12:12:72:539:95:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:have dropout data from 10% of the schools and, reassuringly, the coe-cient onTreat⇥Scoreis the same
21:773:64676:12:12:72:540:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:regardless of the data source used, reflecting a high correlation between measures (0.5). Since the dependent
21:774:64785:12:0:72:466:71:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:variable mean is near 1, Online App. Table G.9 shows robustness to a probit specification.
22:775:64877:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:children whose parents found out they had above-median performance, dropout falls to
22:776:64961:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:nearly 0% (from a control group mean of 2%), whereas it roughly doubles for those with
22:777:65047:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:below-median performance, increasing from 2% to about 4%. These results highlight that
22:778:65133:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:information does not improve educational outcomes for all: it leads to reallocations, which
22:779:65224:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:can decrease investments for some. Since the literature suggests that schooling and ability are
22:780:65319:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:complements, these reallocations are consistent with an improvement in returns (Pitt et al.,
22:781:65411:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:1990; Aizer and Cunha, 2012). In contrast to the results for primary school enrollment, but
22:782:65502:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:perhaps to be expected given parents’ heterogeneous beliefs regarding complementarity with
22:783:65592:18:18:72:539:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performance, I find no significant e↵ects for either expenditures or attendance. See Appendix
22:784:65685:18:30:72:344:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Dforresultsfortwoadditionalsecondaryoutcomes.
22:785:65730:30:19:72:470:516:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:4.4The link between information frictions and poverty
22:786:65783:19:18:95:542:497:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Inowprovideevidencelinkinginformationfrictionswithsocioeconomicstatus(SES)by
22:787:65859:18:18:72:540:479:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:testing for heterogeneity by a measure of SES: parental education. I use parental education
22:788:65950:18:18:72:540:461:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:both because it is the least noisy measure of SES in the data, and because limited education
22:789:66042:18:22:72:528:443:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:provides a potential channel for why low-SES parents are less able to access information.
22:790:66131:22:18:72:424:421:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:Result 4A: Less-educated parents have less accurate beliefs.
