22:800:66858:22:17:72:527:208:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:Result 4B: The e↵ects of information can be larger for less-educated parents.
22:801:66935:17:18:95:539:191:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:I now examine whether, in addition to having less accurate beliefs, less-educated parents
22:802:67024:18:18:72:540:173:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:also respond more to information. I first look at the e↵ects on belief updating, shown in
22:803:67113:18:18:72:540:155:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:column 1 of Panel B of Table 4, which shows the results of estimating equation 1 fully
22:804:67199:18:16:81:539:137:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:27An alternate way to look at belief accuracy is to test whether the absolute value of the gap between
22:805:67301:16:12:72:540:121:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:beliefs and true scores is larger for less-educated parents. Appendix Table A.1 presents the results of this test
22:806:67414:12:12:72:540:109:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:with consistent results. Online Appendix Table G.2 shows robustness to other measures of parent education,
22:807:67520:12:12:72:540:97:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:as well as child performance. Online Appendix Table G.10 shows robustness to controlling for other variables
22:808:67628:12:0:72:441:85:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:and their interactions with score, including school fixed e↵ects interacted with score.
23:809:67717:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:interacted with household-average years of parent education. The results show that less-
23:810:67805:18:18:72:442:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:educated parents update their beliefs more than more-educated parents.
23:811:67875:18:18:95:539:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:We may also wish to know whether this translates into “larger e↵ects” on their deci-
23:812:67959:18:18:72:539:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:sions. Testing this is non-trivial, since it is di-cult to define exactly what a “larger e↵ect” is.
23:813:68058:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:In particular, the magnitude of a parent’s response will depend on her preferred investment
23:814:68149:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:function, which in turn depends on her preferences and budget, both of which may vary
23:815:68234:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:with SES. Some preferred investment functions may be steeper for richer parents, others
23:816:68321:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for poorer parents. To make an “apples to apples” comparison, then, it is useful to focus
23:817:68410:18:18:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:on the investments where the preferred investment function is as homogeneous as possible
23:818:68498:18:18:72:540:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:across parental education levels – and where thus the heterogeneity speaks directly to het-
23:819:68589:18:18:72:539:528:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:erogeneity in the impact of information, since,if there were no gapsin the accuracy and
23:820:68676:18:18:72:540:510:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:uncertainty of parents’ baseline beliefs, there would be no heterogeneity in the results by
23:821:68767:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parental education. The choice of di-culty level of free workbooks is most likely to meet this
23:822:68861:18:17:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:criterion, and was expressly included in the design to provide homogeneity across education
23:823:68952:17:18:72:539:457:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:levels.28Columns (2) and (3) display the results, showing that information has a larger ef-
23:824:69043:18:18:72:540:439:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:fect for less-educated parents. At baseline, the workbook choices of above-median-education
23:825:69134:18:18:72:540:421:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parents are roughly 90% (30%) more steeply sloped for math (English) than the choices of
23:826:69222:18:18:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:below-median-education parents (see positive coe-cient onScore⇥Parent yrs of educ.);
23:827:69306:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:information fully closes the gap (see negativeTreat⇥Score⇥Parent yrs of educ.). See
23:828:69389:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Dizon-Ross (2018) to see the results for the other outcomes, where there is more potential
23:829:69479:18:30:72:466:349:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for heterogeneity in the preferred investment function by parental education.
23:830:69556:30:19:72:376:319:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:4.5Welfare and average treatment e↵ects
23:831:69595:19:18:95:539:300:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:This experiment shows that providing information to parents a↵ects their beliefs and
23:832:69679:18:18:72:540:282:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:decisions. This reveals that parents’ decisions at baseline did not fully incorporate the in-
23:833:69772:18:18:72:539:264:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:formation, and that parents themselves think the information makes them better o↵, i.e.,
23:834:69860:18:18:72:540:246:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that, according to their own (perceived) utility functions, information increases utility. Al-
23:835:69954:18:18:72:540:228:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:though establishing these findings was the key conceptual goal of the paper, one may also
23:836:70043:18:18:72:539:210:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:wonder about the broader welfare implications. Welfare conclusions are di-cult, since any
23:837:70132:18:18:72:540:192:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:intervention that corrects one market imperfection can decrease welfare if there are multiple
23:838:70225:18:18:72:540:174:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:interacting market failures (the “theory of the second best”). Definitive welfare conclusions
23:839:70318:18:17:72:540:156:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:are thus beyond the scope of this paper. That said, I now provide some speculative discussion.
23:840:70412:17:18:95:540:139:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:First, to draw conclusions aboutparents’welfare, we would need to know whether their
23:841:70496:18:16:81:539:121:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:28Since the workbooks are free, the choice should not be confounded by wealth. Moreover, we expect parents
23:842:70602:16:12:72:540:105:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:to choose the workbook di-culty level most closely matching their beliefs about their child’s performance,
23:843:70708:12:12:72:540:93:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:and there is noex  antereason to expect heterogeneity in that behavior by parental education. This is
23:844:70809:12:12:72:539:81:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:corroborated by Online Appendix table G.11: regressions of workbook di-culty level on baseline beliefs in
23:845:70914:12:0:72:485:69:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:the control group show that there is no heterogeneity in that relationship by parent education.
24:846:71011:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:perceived education production function is correct, including how predictive the performance
24:847:71103:18:18:72:539:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:information is for the returns to investment.29Reassuringly, in both developed and developing
24:848:71196:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:country contexts, there is evidence that grades are correlated with other measures of ability,
24:849:71290:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and that grades and achievement tests may even be better predictors of life outcomes (e.g.
24:850:71380:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:wages) than standard measures of ability (Borghans et al. (2011); Sternberg et al. (2001);
24:851:71470:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Borghans et al. (2016)). In addition, for the outcomes that proxy for years of schooling (i.e.,
24:852:71565:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:primary school enrollment and the secondary school lottery), although there are no estimates
24:853:71657:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of the production function in Malawi, estimates from other contexts suggest that years of
24:854:71746:18:18:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:schooling and other measures of ability are complements (Pitt et al., 1990; Aizer and Cunha,
24:855:71838:18:18:72:540:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:2012). Moreover, there are reasons to expect that the complementarity might be greater in
24:856:71927:18:18:72:540:528:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:this setting: the education system in sub-saharan Africa is particularly oriented towards high
24:857:72021:18:18:72:540:510:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performers (Duflo et al., 2011), and achievement tests determine progression through school
24:858:72112:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and access to higher levels of schooling, thus mechanically linking them with returns. My
24:859:72201:18:17:72:540:474:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:finding that parents allocate more years of schooling to their higher performers suggests they
24:860:72295:17:18:72:540:457:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:believe this complementarity exists, and is thereforeconsistentwith parents being correct
24:861:72384:18:18:72:524:439:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:about the production function, but more evidence would be needed for firm conclusions.
24:862:72470:18:18:95:539:421:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Second, to move to social welfare, we would also need to assess both the externalities
24:863:72556:18:18:72:540:403:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of education and the social welfare function. Although no single summary statistic could
24:864:72644:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:fully summarize the welfare impacts, the conventional wisdom is that market imperfections
24:865:72733:18:18:72:540:367:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:(such as positive externalities of education) collectively cause the average level of education
24:866:72828:18:18:72:540:349:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to be below the optimum. As a result, it might be concerning from a welfare perspective if
24:867:72918:18:18:72:540:331:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:providing information about academic performance caused the average level of investments
24:868:73006:18:18:72:540:313:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to fall. Reassuringly, here, information does not appear to decrease the average level of
24:869:73095:18:18:72:540:295:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments, although the results are imprecise. Specifically, Panel A of Appendix Table A.2
24:870:73187:18:18:72:540:277:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:presents the estimates of the average treatment e↵ect (ATE) of information. I do not find
24:871:73276:18:18:72:540:259:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:any statistically significant ATE of information on the investments that could proxy for the
24:872:73368:18:17:72:440:241:143:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f6:B:overall level of investments: enrollment, expenditures, and attendance.30
24:873:73441:17:18:95:539:224:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:One might be surprised by the absence of an ATE for enrollment. Parents on average
24:874:73523:18:18:72:540:206:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:overestimate their children at baseline, and, for enrollment, invest more in higher performers,
24:875:73618:18:18:72:540:188:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:suggesting that information might decrease enrollment. Appendix E describes several poten-
24:876:73708:18:18:72:540:170:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:tial explanations for the lack of an ATE, one of which I find empirical support for: Parents
24:877:73800:18:18:72:540:152:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:respond more to information when the information is positive than when it is negative. This
24:878:73891:18:16:81:539:134:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:29Note that this is much less of a concern when analyzing some of the experimental outcomes (e.g., the
24:879:73993:16:12:72:540:118:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:workbooks and remedial textbooks). These investments were designed to have clear predictions for increased
24:880:74099:12:8:72:519:106:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:returns, and, across the parental education spectrum, parents’ reallocations align with the predictions.
24:881:74203:8:15:81:539:98:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:30The workbooks and textbooks were designed specifically to look at thetypesof investment chosen, and
24:882:74304:15:12:72:540:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:thus their level does not proxy for overall spending. For completeness, however, these ATEs are also reported
24:883:74413:12:0:72:175:71:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:in Appendix Table A.2.
25:884:74437:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:is consistent with the findings of the motivated beliefs literature (Eil and Rao, 2011; Mobius
25:885:74531:18:31:72:510:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and Rosenblat, 2014). See Appendix E and Table A.3 for the analysis and discussion.
25:886:74614:31:19:72:194:659:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:4.6Mechanisms
25:887:74627:19:17:95:539:640:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Results 1-4 clearly show that providing student performance information to parents af-
25:888:74713:17:18:72:540:623:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:fects their decisions. Are there any explanations for this besides the fact that information
25:889:74805:18:18:72:540:605:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:changes parents’ beliefs about their children’s academic performance? One potential alterna-
25:890:74897:18:18:72:540:587:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:tive explanation is that information a↵ects thesalienceof academic performance. However,
25:891:74985:18:18:72:539:569:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:assuming salience e↵ects are uniform across the population, they should a↵ect the investment
25:892:75077:18:18:72:452:551:143:g_d0_f9:64:g_d0_f6:C:level,nottheslope,sowouldnotberesponsibleforthee↵ectsseenhere.31
25:893:75141:18:18:95:543:533:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Arelatedquestioniswhetherinformationa↵ectsinvestmentsprimarilybya↵ectingthe
25:894:75216:18:18:72:540:515:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:mean or the uncertainty of parents’ beliefs distributions. I investigate this in Appendix F.
25:895:75308:18:18:72:539:497:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:The analyses suggest that the primary mechanism for information’s e↵ects on thetypesof
25:896:75394:18:18:72:540:479:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments chosen (e.g., di-culty levels of workbooks) is changes to the mean/accuracy of
25:897:75484:18:18:72:540:461:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:beliefs, but that changes in the uncertainty of beliefs also play a role for the larger investments
25:898:75583:18:35:72:296:443:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that proxy more for thelevelof investment.
25:899:75625:35:22:72:194:408:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:C:5Conclusion
25:900:75636:22:18:95:539:386:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:This paper highlights an important source of misinformation that a↵ects decisions: par-
25:901:75723:18:18:72:540:368:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ents’ inaccurate beliefs about their children’s academic performance. I show that (perceived)
25:902:75816:18:18:72:540:350:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:academic performance is an important input into parents’ investment decisions, but that
25:903:75903:18:18:72:540:332:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:despite the ready availability of academic performance information, many parents’ beliefs
25:904:75992:18:17:72:540:314:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:about their children’s academic performance are quite wrong – with important consequences
25:905:76081:17:18:72:540:297:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for the allocation of educational investments. Providing academic performance information
25:906:76170:18:18:72:540:279:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to parents causes them to change both thelevelandtypeof investments they choose for their
25:907:76259:18:18:72:540:261:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:children. The impacts are seen across a broad range of investments, from those with very
25:908:76347:18:18:72:540:243:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:clean predictions about how parents should invest to maximize returns (e.g., remedial text-
25:909:76438:18:18:72:540:225:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:books that are more useful for low-performing students), to more consequential investments
25:910:76528:18:18:72:307:207:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that proxy for overall educational attainment.
25:911:76574:18:18:95:539:189:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:It is perhaps surprising that baseline information is poor if the returns to knowledge are
25:912:76664:18:18:72:540:171:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:high and the information is, in principle, readily available. But, parents may over-estimate
25:913:76756:18:18:72:540:153:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:their own knowledge, or the (perceived) costs of acquiring information may be high, es-
25:914:76843:18:18:72:540:135:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:pecially for uneducated or illiterate parents. Indeed, interviews with parents suggest that
25:915:76934:18:15:81:539:117:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:31If salience e↵ects vary and are correlated with performance, this could a↵ect the slope. But, salience
25:916:77038:15:12:72:539:102:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:would likely be a household-level e↵ect, or correlated with child-level controls. Online Appendix Tables
25:917:77142:12:12:72:540:90:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:G.12 and G.13, which show robustness to household fixed e↵ects and to controlling for child-level controls
25:918:77248:12:12:72:540:78:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:interacted with treatment, thus assuage the concern. For dropouts, we lose statistical power quickly, but the
25:919:77357:12:0:72:376:66:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:coe-cient for enrollment stays stable and the p-value remains0.15.
26:920:77426:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:uneducated parents are intimidated to talk with their children’s teachers. These barriers to
26:921:77518:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:accessing information may be more pervasive in poorer countries and among poorer house-
26:922:77605:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:holds. Consistent with this, I find that less-educated parents in my setting have less accurate
26:923:77700:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:beliefs. This same pattern is also evident in beliefs data from other contexts, including the
26:924:77793:18:18:72:508:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:U.S.,32and suggests a potential link between poor access to information and poverty.
26:925:77877:18:18:95:539:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:This paper focused on identifying the causal chain between parents’ beliefs and their
26:926:77962:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments. One area for future research would be to extend the causal chain further to
26:927:78050:18:18:72:540:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:better understand the link between investments and welfare, for example by measuring the
26:928:78138:18:18:72:540:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:objective returns to di↵erent educational investments and comparing them with parents’
26:929:78224:18:18:72:540:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:perceptions. A second direction for future work would be to design and test a scalable
26:930:78310:18:460:72:253:528:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:information-dissemination strategy.
26:931:78345:460:0:81:473:68:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:32U.S. data were provided by Alexander and Entwisle (2006) and analyzed by the author.

36:1310:98158:13:13:94:698:165:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:Score) to see how much the slope has increased as a result of information. Take for example column (2). The ratio of the coe-cient on Treat
36:1311:98297:13:13:94:697:152:99:g_d0_f15:99:g_d0_f8:F:⇥Score (1.34) to the coe-cient on Score (0.65) shows us that the slope has increased by roughly 200% (1.34/0.65), so that the treatment
36:1312:98432:13:13:94:698:139:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:slope is roughly 3 times as large as the control slope. The rough interpretation of the slope in the control group for that column is that, if
36:1313:98574:13:13:94:698:126:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:the child’s math score increases by one point, the chance that her parent chooses the next higher di-culty level of the free book increases

46:1630:114468:31:19:72:279:515:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:C.2Uncertainty predictions
46:1631:114494:19:18:95:539:496:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:There are many ways to model uncertainty in beliefs. Here, I show one potential frame-
46:1632:114580:18:18:72:540:478:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:work which yields the prediction that uncertainty in parents’ beliefs about academic perfor-
46:1633:114672:18:18:72:544:460:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:mance leads to attenuation in the slope of investments on mean beliefs↵.Theframework
46:1634:114756:18:18:72:540:442:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:captures the intuition described in the main text: that uncertainty in parents’ beliefs may
46:1635:114847:18:18:72:540:424:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:make them hesitate to make their investments depend as strongly on their mean beliefs. This
46:1636:114938:18:18:72:321:406:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:is a richer model than the one used in Section 2.
46:1637:114987:18:17:95:539:388:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Assume there is some true unobserved underlying academic skill. Call thisaand call
46:1638:115069:17:18:72:539:371:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parents’ beliefs about it↵. Assume this underlying academic skill is what determines returns
46:1639:115161:18:18:72:540:353:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and is thus what parents truly want to base decisions on. Assume further that academic skill
46:1640:115253:18:18:72:540:335:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:is distinct from academic performance,a,whereais what we measured baseline beliefs on,
46:1641:115339:18:18:72:540:317:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:and what we delivered information about in the intervention; instead, academic performance
46:1642:115429:18:18:72:263:299:143:g_d0_f10:143:g_d0_f4:B:ais taken by parents as a signal ofa.
46:1643:115466:18:18:95:540:281:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:In this context, we can model beliefs about academic skill↵as being a convex combi-
46:1644:115549:18:18:72:540:263:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:nation of beliefs about school performance,↵, and beliefs about all other aspects or signals
46:1645:115641:18:36:72:246:245:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of academic skills,↵-↵,givenby:
46:1646:115672:36:26:250:360:209:143:g_d0_f37:64:g_d0_f13:C:↵=-↵+(1--)↵-↵
46:1647:115685:26:18:72:338:183:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:where-is the weight on the academic performance.
46:1648:115733:18:18:95:544:165:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Since preferred investments would be a function of↵,not↵,wecouldwritethepre-
46:1649:115809:18:18:72:539:147:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ferred investment function as  ̃s⇤(↵). For expositional simplicity, let’s look at the linear case
46:1650:115906:18:18:72:539:129:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:where  ̃s⇤(↵)= ̃-0+ ̃-1↵(where the ̃-1notation distinguishes this from the preferred invest-
46:1651:115998:18:16:81:539:111:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:35Note that this assumes that parents fully update their beliefs in response to the intervention. If they
46:1652:116103:16:12:72:539:95:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:only partially update their beliefs, then the di↵erence in slope between treatment and control groups would
46:1653:116210:12:14:72:540:83:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:be weighted downwards by the updating parameter (i.e., if updated beliefs were a weighted combination of
46:1654:116314:14:0:72:491:69:99:g_d0_f17:99:g_d0_f8:F:aand↵with-the weight ona, then the di↵erence in slopes would uncover-(-1--1cov(↵,a)var(a))).
47:1655:116408:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ment function in the simpler model from Section 2 and Appendix Section C.1.) Preferred
47:1656:116494:18:34:72:264:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments could then be written as:
47:1657:116531:34:21:216:306:656:143:g_d0_f10:143:g_d0_f37:C:s⇤(↵)= ̃-0+ ̃-1↵
47:1658:116547:21:33:248:394:635:143:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f13:A:= ̃-0+ ̃-1-↵+ ̃-1(1--)↵-↵
47:1659:116572:33:18:72:544:602:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:In this context, providing information about academic performance,a,shouldincreasethe
47:1660:116657:18:18:72:539:584:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:certainty of parents’ beliefs distributions (i.e., decrease-2). This could increase the weight

47:1662:116840:18:18:72:540:548:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:underlying academic skill↵,thatis,increase-.Since-increases, under most assumptions for

47:1668:117267:36:22:72:374:422:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:C:DResults for secondary outcomes
47:1669:117298:22:18:95:539:400:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:In the endline survey, I also collected data on two outcomes which I considered sec-
47:1670:117382:18:18:72:539:382:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ondary because I did not haveex antehypotheses that there would be e↵ects or because

47:1674:117727:18:18:72:540:310:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:vestments would respond to their children’s performance, but expected power was low since
47:1675:117816:18:18:72:540:292:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:it is di-cult to measure these investments cleanly. I find positive average treatment e↵ects,
47:1676:117909:18:17:72:540:274:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:but no significant impact on the slope. For transfers across schools, parents did not indicate
47:1677:118003:17:18:72:539:257:143:g_d0_f9:143:g_d0_f4:B:ex antethat it was a margin which would respond. However, information increases transfers
47:1678:118092:18:18:72:540:239:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:(defined as an indicator that the child transferred schools, not conditional on enrollment) by
47:1679:118186:18:18:72:540:221:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:50%, from 6% to 9%. Although there is no change in the slope on performance, heterogeneity
47:1680:118276:18:18:72:540:203:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:in the preferred slope by school type could explain this. At low-quality schools, finding out a
47:1681:118371:18:20:72:539:185:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:child is doing well might make it worth the e↵ort costs of changing him to a better school, so
47:1682:118465:20:7:81:480:165:49:g_d0_f7:49:g_d0_f7:F:36Specifically, the regression of investments on↵would have slope--1+(1--)-1cov(↵,↵-↵)
47:1683:118551:7:13:446:540:158:49:g_d0_f18:99:g_d0_f15:F:Var(↵)=--1+(1-
47:1684:118565:13:13:72:540:145:99:g_d0_f36:99:g_d0_f8:F:-)-1corr(↵,↵-↵)sd(↵-↵)sd(↵).Thus,sincecorr(↵,↵-↵)1,increasing-should increase the slope as long as
47:1685:118664:13:8:72:362:132:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:the variance of↵-↵is not too much larger than the variance of↵.
47:1686:118727:8:16:81:539:124:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:37For example, with a linear preferred investment function and a quadratic loss function, the slope of the
47:1687:118833:16:12:72:540:108:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:true preferred investment function should not change. It is useful to note that in this richer model, although
47:1688:118943:12:12:72:540:96:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:providing information aboutashould unambiguously increase the certainty of↵, it is ambiguous whether
47:1689:119043:12:12:72:539:84:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:it will decrease or increase the uncertainty of beliefs abouta. For example, if the information were very
47:1690:119148:12:0:72:453:72:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:di↵erent from parents’ prior beliefs, it could increase the uncertainty of beliefs abouta.
48:1691:119240:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:transfers would be positively sloped with performance. In contrast, at high-quality schools,
48:1692:119332:18:18:72:540:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:finding out a child is doing poorly could indicate a poor match, and so transfers would have
48:1693:119424:18:18:72:540:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the opposite slope. Indeed, if we look at the results separately by school quality (proxied by
48:1694:119518:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:school-average achievement), there are slope e↵ects, with the slope becoming more positive
48:1695:119608:18:18:72:540:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:at low-quality schools and more negative at high-quality schools (Online Appendix Table
48:1696:119695:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:G.15). Of course, this is just one of many potential explanations – and it implicitly assumes
48:1697:119788:18:36:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:that parents know school quality, which may not be the case – but the results are suggestive.
48:1698:119881:36:22:72:540:564:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:C:EDiscussion of the absence of an ATE for enrollment
48:1699:119932:22:18:95:539:542:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Parents on average overestimate their children’s performance at baseline, and, for en-
48:1700:120018:18:18:72:540:524:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:rollment, invest more in their higher performers. This suggests that providing information
48:1701:120108:18:18:72:540:506:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:might decrease enrollment. However, we do not find a significant e↵ect. There are several
48:1702:120197:18:18:72:540:488:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:potential (non-mutually-exclusive) explanations. First, uncertainty in the control group may
48:1703:120289:18:18:72:540:470:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:decrease investment, akin to uncertainty dampening investment in risky assets. However, I
48:1704:120378:18:18:72:540:452:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:do not observe a positive average level e↵ect for the parents who had more accurate beliefs
48:1705:120469:18:18:72:540:434:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:at baseline, though the power of the test is low (see Panel B of Appendix Table A.2). Sec-
48:1706:120559:18:18:72:539:416:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ond, parents may already be spending as much as they can on education, and so the e↵ect
48:1707:120646:18:18:72:540:398:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of information is primarily on the allocation of spending, not the level. Unfortunately this
48:1708:120738:18:18:72:539:380:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:channel is di-cult to test. Third, parents’ reported beliefs may be biased upwards somewhat
48:1709:120829:18:18:72:539:362:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:relative to true beliefs. This channel is also unfortunately di-cult to test. Fourth, parents
48:1710:120922:18:18:72:540:344:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:could respond more to positive than to negative information; I explore this channel in detail
48:1711:121015:18:22:72:319:326:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:below. Finally, we may lack statistical precision.
48:1712:121065:22:18:72:470:304:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:Result: Investments respond more to positive than negative shocks.
48:1713:121131:18:18:95:539:286:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Appendix Table A.3 shows the results from estimating equation 1, fully interacted with
48:1714:121217:18:18:72:540:268:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:a dummy for receiving a positive information shock (Aij> ̃Aij). The model is estimated
48:1715:121303:18:18:72:540:250:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for all outcomes for which (a) one direction of shock is unambiguously positive (e.g., the
48:1716:121393:18:18:72:540:232:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:secondary school lottery depends on between-child performance and so neither direction is
48:1717:121482:18:18:72:540:214:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:“positive”; thus, that outcome is not included); and (b) there is a treatment e↵ect on the
48:1718:121572:18:18:72:544:196:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:slope in the full sample. The change in slope (coe-cient onT reat⇥Score)islargerfor
48:1719:121655:18:18:72:538:178:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:parents who receive positive information shocks.38For enrollment, precision is lacking, but
48:1720:121746:18:18:72:539:160:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the magnitude of the coe-cient is large, suggesting that this channel could help explain why
48:1721:121838:18:17:72:280:142:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:there is no negative ATE for enrollment.
48:1722:121878:17:16:81:539:125:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:38It would potentially be concerning if the positive information shocks were larger, but that is not the case:
48:1723:121988:16:12:72:540:109:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:The absolute gap between believed and true performance is roughly 40% smaller for the positive information
48:1724:122094:12:12:72:540:97:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:shock sample. Another potential concern is that some actions are bounded (e.g., one cannot choose a less
48:1725:122198:12:12:72:539:85:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:di-cult workbook than beginner), but restricting the sample to parents whose predicted behavior (based on
48:1726:122303:12:0:72:460:73:99:g_d0_f8:99:g_d0_f8:F:baseline beliefs) is in the middle of the range of potential outcomes yields similar results.
49:1727:122398:0:22:72:497:700:296:g_d0_f3:296:g_d0_f3:C:FMechanisms: The role of uncertainty in beliefs
49:1728:122445:22:18:95:539:678:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:My primary analyses show that information increases the slope of investments on true
49:1729:122529:18:18:72:540:660:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:performance, thus suggesting that the slope was attenuated at baseline. As discussed in
49:1730:122616:18:18:72:540:642:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Section 2, both inaccuracies in the mean of baseline beliefs and uncertainty of baseline beliefs
49:1731:122712:18:18:72:540:624:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:could cause that baseline attenuation. A reasonable question is thus whether the channel for
49:1732:122804:18:18:72:539:606:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the treatment e↵ects is an e↵ect on the mean or on the uncertainty of beliefs. The analysis
49:1733:122895:18:18:72:540:588:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of the channels is suggestive in nature, since I did not experimentally vary uncertainty
49:1734:122983:18:18:72:540:570:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:separately from the mean, nor (for budget reasons) did I measure uncertainty at endline.
49:1735:123071:18:18:72:540:552:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Under an uncertainty channel, uncertainty could decrease the preferred slope of investments
49:1736:123162:18:18:72:539:534:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:as a function of meanbeliefs, since parents may not want to invest as steeply based on their
49:1737:123254:18:18:72:539:516:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:mean beliefs if their beliefs are uncertain.39The attenuation of preferred investments on
49:1738:123343:18:18:72:540:498:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:beliefs would then cause attenuation of actual investments ontrueperformance – which is
49:1739:123430:18:17:72:540:480:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the attenuation that has been the focus of the analysis so far. In contrast, under the channel
49:1740:123524:17:18:72:540:463:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of inaccurate means, the slope of investments as a function of mean beliefs is not attenuated;
49:1741:123618:18:18:72:540:445:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:rather, the attenuation of investments on true performance stems from the fact that, because
49:1742:123710:18:18:72:540:427:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:beliefs are inaccurate, they themselves are attenuated functions of true performance. As a
49:1743:123800:18:18:72:540:409:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:result, one empirical signature of the uncertainty channel is attenuation of investments on
49:1744:123891:18:18:72:539:391:143:g_d0_f9:143:g_d0_f4:B:beliefsthemselves; to assess uncertainty’s role, I test whether information increases the slope
49:1745:123986:18:18:72:540:373:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of investments on beliefs. I use two approaches; both suggest that the primary mechanism
49:1746:124074:18:18:72:539:355:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for reallocations acrosstypesof investments (e.g., di-culty levels of workbooks) is changes
49:1747:124165:18:18:72:540:337:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:to the mean/accuracy of beliefs, but that changes to the uncertainty of beliefs matter more
49:1748:124256:18:18:72:431:319:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for the larger investments that proxy more for thelevelof investment.
49:1749:124325:18:18:95:540:301:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:The first approach looks at the treatment e↵ect on the slope for those who have relatively
49:1750:124415:18:18:72:540:283:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:accurate beliefs at baseline. For this group, there is no belief accuracy e↵ect of information
49:1751:124509:18:18:72:540:265:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:(since beliefs were accurate to begin with). Any slope change therefore will likely represent an
49:1752:124605:18:18:72:540:247:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:uncertainty e↵ect. Panel A of Appendix Table A.4 shows the results of estimating equation
49:1753:124694:18:17:72:544:229:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:1forparentswhosebeliefsregardingtheirchildren’sperformancewerewithin10pointsof
49:1754:124772:17:18:72:540:212:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the true score. For the smaller investments, such as workbooks, the slope for these parents
49:1755:124863:18:18:72:540:194:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:changes a little (i.e., there is a small uncertainty e↵ect), but the e↵ect is only 30% of the
49:1756:124956:18:18:72:540:176:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:magnitude – and significantly di↵erent from – the change in slope in the full sample. This
49:1757:125046:18:18:72:539:158:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:suggests that the e↵ect presented earlier for the full sample is driven primarily by changes to
49:1758:125141:18:18:72:540:140:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:belief accuracy. This is not surprising, since the preferred investment function was already
49:1759:125233:18:18:72:540:122:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:steeply sloped in the control group. For the larger investments, on the other hand, the
49:1760:125320:18:18:72:540:104:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:uncertainty e↵ects are larger, with e↵ects in the accurate beliefs sample representing 50%
49:1761:125410:18:18:72:540:86:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:of the coe-cient estimated in the full sample for the lottery, and 100% for enrollment. Of
49:1762:125500:18:0:81:347:68:49:g_d0_f7:99:g_d0_f8:F:39See Appendix C.2 for a framework yielding this prediction.
50:1763:125562:0:18:72:540:708:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:course, a key caveat to interpretation is that parents with accurate beliefs could be di↵erent
50:1764:125656:18:18:72:430:690:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:from other parents; for example, they could have more certain beliefs.
50:1765:125726:18:18:95:544:672:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Asecondapproachistotestwhethertheheterogeneityinthetreatmente↵ectbyper-
50:1766:125797:18:18:72:540:654:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:formance is equal and opposite to the heterogeneity by baseline beliefs. Suppose preferred
50:1767:125887:18:18:72:545:636:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investments as a function of baseline beliefs take the form-0+-1↵.Ifinformationdoes
50:1768:125970:18:18:72:540:618:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:not change thepreferredslope, this means that information simply moves parents along
50:1769:126054:18:18:72:540:600:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the preferred function by the amount of the information shock (a-↵). In that case, the
50:1770:126140:18:18:72:539:582:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:treatment e↵ect would be-1(a-↵), and the coe-cients onT reat⇥aandT reat⇥↵would
50:1771:126218:18:18:72:543:564:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:be equal and opposite:-1and--1,respectively.If,instead,themagnitudeofthecoe-cient
50:1772:126299:18:18:72:543:546:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:onT reat⇥ais larger than that ofT reat⇥↵,itsuggeststhatbeliefsaboutacademicper-
50:1773:126378:18:18:72:540:528:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:formance are more important to treatment parents’ investments than to control parents’,
50:1774:126465:18:18:72:540:510:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:i.e., the slope of investments on beliefs has increased. To see this, denote the slope of the
50:1775:126558:18:18:72:540:492:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:investment function in the control (treatment) group-C1(-1). Parentiwith baseline beliefs
50:1776:126647:18:17:72:539:474:143:g_d0_f19:143:g_d0_f4:B:↵iand true performanceaiwould have investment ofsC(↵i)=-C0+-C1↵iin the control
50:1777:126725:17:18:72:539:457:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:group, ands(ai)=-0+-1aiin the treatment group. Thus, the treatment e↵ect as a function
50:1778:126811:18:18:72:544:439:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:ofaand↵is⌧(ai,↵i)=s(ai)-sC(↵i)=(-0--C0)+-1ai--C1↵i,andsoheterogeneityin
50:1779:126882:18:18:72:466:421:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the treatment e↵ect byaidentifies-1and heterogeneity by↵identifies--C1.
50:1780:126953:18:18:95:539:403:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:Panel B of Appendix Table A.4 shows that the results are consistent with the previous
50:1781:127038:18:18:72:540:385:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:test, since the lottery and enrollment are the only investments where we can reject that the
50:1782:127130:18:18:72:258:367:143:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f6:B:coe-cients are equal and opposite.40
50:1783:127166:18:18:95:538:349:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:To assess whether these slope changes do in fact reflect uncertainty, I can look at hetero-
50:1784:127257:18:18:72:540:331:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:geneity in both of the above tests by a baseline measure of the uncertainty of beliefs. Power is
50:1785:127353:18:18:72:539:313:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:low and so the results are somewhat inconclusive; reassuringly, however, the only coe-cient
50:1786:127444:18:18:72:540:295:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:significant at the 10% level (English workbooks) does suggest that the slope increases more
50:1787:127535:18:18:72:450:277:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:for parents with more uncertain beliefs. See Online Appendix Table G.16.
50:1788:127607:18:18:95:540:259:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:A:This section focused on a specific e↵ect of uncertainty on investments, namely, whether
50:1789:127694:18:17:72:539:241:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:changes to uncertainty contributed to the core treatment e↵ects analyzed in this paper:
50:1790:127781:17:18:72:540:224:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:the treatment e↵ects of information on the alignment of investments with performance.
50:1791:127866:18:18:72:539:206:143:g_d0_f4:143:g_d0_f4:B:Uncertainty can also a↵ect investments in other ways that are not the focus of this paper
